[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  *     * Features\n    * Who can use the Fogify Framework?\n  * What can you do with Fogify?\n    * Topology Editing\n    * Deployment\n    * Testing\n    * Analysis\n  * Screenshots and Images\n  * Who is using it?\n  * Resources\n    * The Team\n    * Publications\n    * Videos\n    * Awards & Acknowledgements\n\n# Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework\n\nFogify is an emulation Framework easing the modeling, deployment and\nexperimentation of fog testbeds. Fogify provides a toolset to: model complex\nfog topologies comprised of heterogeneous resources, network capabilities and\nQoS criteria; deploy the modelled configuration and services using popular\ncontainerized infrastructure-as-code descriptions to a cloud or local\nenvironment; experiment, measure and evaluate the deployment by injecting\nfaults and adapting the configuration at runtime to test different "what-if"\nscenarios that reveal the limitations of a service before introduced to the\npublic.\n\n* * *\n\n### Features\n\n#####  Resources Heterogeneity\n\nFogify is able to emulate Fog nodes with heterogeneous resources and\ncapabilities.\n\n####  Network Links Heterogeneity\n\nControlling the link quality, such as network latency, bandwidth, error rate,\netc.,and even reproduce real-world node-to-node and node-to-network connection\ntraces\n\n#####  Controllable Faults and Alterations\n\nChanges on running topology by injecting faults, alter network quality,and\ninject (varying) workload and compute resources\n\n####  Any-scale Experimentation\n\nScalability from topologies with a limited number of nodes, capable to run on\na single laptop or PC, tohundreds or thousands nodes, running on a whole\ncluster.\n\n####  Monitoring Capabilities\n\nCollect, manage, and process metrics from emulated Fog Nodes, network\nconnections, and application-level information seamlessly\n\n#####  Rapid Application Deployment\n\nFunctional prototypes of an applications, written in docker-compose, demand no\nmodifications to its business logic in order run on Fogify.\n\n* * *\n\n### Who can use the Fogify Framework?\n\n####  IoT Service Developers\n\nwho wish to ease the testing of their services in geo-distributed fog\nsettings. With the proposed stack, developers design fog enabled services by\nusing Fogify to rapidly perform multiple tests and compare both well-\nfunctionality and performance.\n\n####  Academic Researchers\n\nwho wish to quickly assess algorithms for fog realms. Such users want to\nquickly perform their analysis over system prototypes, testing scenarios and\nfog settings, to discover insights without time and cost overheads of having\nto deploy prototypes over geo-distributed infrastructure.\n\n####  Fog Computing Operators\n\nwho wish to assess the impact of IoT devices to their infrastructure before\npurchasing and deploying to production.\n\n* * *\n\n## What can you do with Fogify?\n\n### Topology Editing\n\nA typical workflow starts with the user editing the docker-compose file of an\nIoT application, and extend it to encapsulate Fogify\'s model. The Fogify model\nis composed of: (i) _Fog Templates_ , allowing the description of _Services_ ,\n_Nodes_ and _Networks_ ; and (ii) the _Fog Topology_ , enabling users to\nspecify _Blueprints_. A Blueprint represents an emulated device and is a\ncombination of a _Node_ , _Service_ , _Networks_ , _replicas_ and a _label_.\nServices are inherited from docker-compose while the _x-fogify_ section\nprovides all Fogify primitives. Thus, users still develop their application\nusing familiar docker constructs with the added functionality of Fogify not\naffecting portability. This means that a Fogify enhanced description will run\nin any docker runtime environment without any alterations, however users will\nlose the functionality offered by Fogify.\n\n### Deployment\n\nWhen the description is ready, the user deploys the application using the\nFogifySDK through a Jupyter notebook, with the description received by the\nFogify Controller. If no error is detected by the Controller, it spawns the\nemulated devices and creates the overlay mesh networks between them,\ninstantiates the services, and broadcasts (any) network constraints to Fogify\nAgents. Specifically, the Controller translates the model specification to\nunderlying orchestration primitives and deploys them via the Cluster\nOrchestrator, ensuring the instantiation of the containerized services on the\nemulated environment. Located on every cluster node, Fogify Agents expose an\nAPI to accept requests from the Controller, apply network QoS primitives, and\nmonitor the emulated devices.\n\n### Testing\n\nOn a running emulated deployment, Fogify enables developers to apply _Actions_\nand "what-if" _Scenarios_ (sequences of timestamped actions) on their IoT\nservices, such as ad-hoc faults and topology changes. Actions and Scenarios\nare written by following the Fogify _Runtime Evaluation Model_. When an action\nor a scenario is submitted, the Fogify Controller coordinates its execution\nwith the Cluster Orchestrator and the respective Fogify Agents. Furthermore,\nFogify captures performance and app-level metrics via the Fogify Agent\nmonitoring module. All metrics are stored at the Agent\'s local storage and can\nbe retrieved from the FogifySDK.\n\n### Analysis\n\nTo create an end-to-end interactive analytic tool for emulated deployments, we\nexploit the FogifySDK capabilities in Jupyter Notebook stack. Specifically, we\npre-installed the FogifySDK library on Jupyter thus the user can (un-) deploy\na Fog Topology, apply ad-hoc changes and scenarios, and, especially, retrieve\nruntime performance metrics. For the latter, FogifySDK stores metrics to an\nin-memory data structure, namely panda\'s dataframe, providing exploratory\nanalysis methods that produce plots and summary statistics. Except of out-of-\nthe-box plots, provided by Pandas, we extended FogifySDK with tailored\nfunctions that provide a set of plots illustrating and explaining the effects\nof actions and scenarios in application performance. With the wide range of\nanalytic methods provided by FogifySDK, users extract useful insights about\nQoS, cost, and predictive analytics. Finally, users may integrate other\nlibraries, like scikit-learn, to endrose their analysis with ML and AI models.\n\n* * *\n\n## Screenshots and Images\n\n##### **Fogify Overview**\n\n##### **Fogify integration with Jupyter**\n\n## Who is using it?\n\n* * *\n\n## Resources\n\n### The Team\n\nThe creators of the Fogify are members of the Laboratory for Internet\nComputing (LInC), University of Cyprus. You can find more information about\nour research activity visit our publications\' page and our on-going projects.\n\n### Publications\n\nFor more details about Fogify and our scientific contributions, you can read\nthe papers of Fogify and a published Demo. Fogify provides a toolset to: model complex\nfog topologies comprised of heterogeneous resources, network capabilities and\nQoS criteria; deploy the modelled configuration and services using popular\ncontainerized infrastructure-as-code descriptions to a cloud or local\nenvironment; experiment, measure and evaluate the deployment by injecting\nfaults and adapting the configuration at runtime to test different "what-if"\nscenarios that reveal the limitations of a service before introduced to the\npublic.\n\n### Topology Editing\n\nA typical workflow starts with the user editing the docker-compose file of an\nIoT application, and extend it to encapsulate Fogify\'s model. The Fogify model\nis composed of: (i) _Fog Templates_ , allowing the description of _Services_ ,\n_Nodes_ and _Networks_ ; and (ii) the _Fog Topology_ , enabling users to\nspecify _Blueprints_. A Blueprint represents an emulated device and is a\ncombination of a _Node_ , _Service_ , _Networks_ , _replicas_ and a _label_.\nServices are inherited from docker-compose while the _x-fogify_ section\nprovides all Fogify primitives. Thus, users still develop their application\nusing familiar docker constructs with the added functionality of Fogify not\naffecting portability. This means that a Fogify enhanced description will run\nin any docker runtime environment without any alterations, however users will\nlose the functionality offered by Fogify.\n\n### Deployment\n\nWhen the description is ready, the user deploys the application using the\nFogifySDK through a Jupyter notebook, with the description received by the\nFogify Controller. If no error is detected by the Controller, it spawns the\nemulated devices and creates the overlay mesh networks between them,\ninstantiates the services, and broadcasts (any) network constraints to Fogify\nAgents. Specifically, the Controller translates the model specification to\nunderlying orchestration primitives and deploys them via the Cluster\nOrchestrator, ensuring the instantiation of the containerized services on the\nemulated environment. Located on every cluster node, Fogify Agents expose an\nAPI to accept requests from the Controller, apply network QoS primitives, and\nmonitor the emulated devices.\n\n### Testing\n\nOn a running emulated deployment, Fogify enables developers to apply _Actions_\nand "what-if" _Scenarios_ (sequences of timestamped actions) on their IoT\nservices, such as ad-hoc faults and topology changes. Actions and Scenarios\nare written by following the Fogify _Runtime Evaluation Model_. When an action\nor a scenario is submitted, the Fogify Controller coordinates its execution\nwith the Cluster Orchestrator and the respective Fogify Agents. Furthermore,\nFogify captures performance and app-level metrics via the Fogify Agent\nmonitoring module. All metrics are stored at the Agent\'s local storage and can\nbe retrieved from the FogifySDK.\n\n### Analysis\n\nTo create an end-to-end interactive analytic tool for emulated deployments, we\nexploit the FogifySDK capabilities in Jupyter Notebook stack. Specifically, we\npre-installed the FogifySDK library on Jupyter thus the user can (un-) deploy\na Fog Topology, apply ad-hoc changes and scenarios, and, especially, retrieve\nruntime performance metrics. For the latter, FogifySDK stores metrics to an\nin-memory data structure, namely panda\'s dataframe, providing exploratory\nanalysis methods that produce plots and summary statistics. Except of out-of-\nthe-box plots, provided by Pandas, we extended FogifySDK with tailored\nfunctions that provide a set of plots illustrating and explaining the effects\nof actions and scenarios in application performance. With the wide range of\nanalytic methods provided by FogifySDK, users extract useful insights about\nQoS, cost, and predictive analytics. Finally, users may integrate other\nlibraries, like scikit-learn, to endrose their analysis with ML and AI models.\n\n## Resources\n\n### Documentation\n\nYou will find the full documentation of the Fogify at the documentation page.\nAt Fogify\'s documentation, we provide details about installation, modeling,\nexperimentation, and, generally, a full get-started guide about the project.\n\n### The Team\n\nThe creators of the Fogify are members of the Laboratory for Internet\nComputing (LInC), University of Cyprus. You can find more information about\nour research activity visit our publications\' page and our on-going projects.\n\n### Publications\n\nFor more details about Fogify and our scientific contributions, you can read\nthe papers of Fogify and a published Demo. If you would like to use Fogify for\nyour research, you should include at least on of the following BibTeX entries.\n\nFogify\'s paper BibTeX citation:\n\n    \n    \n    @inproceedings{Symeonides2020,\n    author    = {Moysis, Symeonides and Zacharias, Georgiou and Demetris, Trihinas and George, Pallis and Marios D., Dikaiakos},\n    title     = {Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework},\n    year      = {2020},\n    publisher = {Association for Computing Machinery},\n    address   = {New York, NY, USA},\n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 5th ACM/IEEE Symposium on Edge Computing},\n    location  = {San Jose, CA, USA},\n    series    = {SEC ’20}\n    }\n    \n\nFogify\'s demo BibTeX citation:\n\n    \n    \n    @inproceedings{Symeonides2020,\n    author    = {Moysis, Symeonides and Zacharias, Georgiou and Demetris, Trihinas and George, Pallis and Marios D., Dikaiakos},\n    title     = {Demo: Emulating Geo-Distributed Fog Services},\n    year      = {2020},\n    publisher = {Association for Computing Machinery},\n    address   = {New York, NY, USA},\n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 5th ACM/IEEE Symposium on Edge Computing},\n    location  = {San Jose, CA, USA},\n    series    = {SEC ’20}\n    } \n    \n\n### Acknowledgements\n\nThis work is partially supported by the EU Commission through RAINBOW 871403\n(ICT-15-2019-2020) project and by the Cyprus Research and Innovation\nFoundation through COMPLEMENTARY/0916/0916/0171 project.\n\n### License\n\nThe framework is open-sourced under the Apache 2.0 License base. To alleviate the\ndifficulties in setting up real-world 5G testbeds, we introduce 5G-Slicer\nextension of the Fogify framework. 5G-Slicer facilitates the definition of\nmobile network slices through modeling abstractions for radio units, mobile\nnodes, trajectories, etc., while also offering realistic network QoS by\ndynamically altering -at runtime- signal strength. Moreover, 5G-Slicer\nprovides an already realized scenario for a city-scale deployment that smart-\ncity researchers can simply configure through a "ready-to-use" template,\nleaving 5G-Slicer responsible for translating it into an emulated environment.\n\n* * *\n\n## System Overview\n\nA typical deployment starts by either describing the application services and\nnetwork fabric via the 5G-Slicer model specification or by parameterizing a\n"ready-to-use" testbed template. The model specification can denote a wide\nrange of network slice parameters, including the position of compute nodes and\nRUs, network links and their QoS, mobile node traces, communication protocols\nand VNFs applicable on nodes. On the contrary, parametrizable use-case\ntemplates automatically produce 5G deployments for IoT applications. The\noutput of each template is a programming view equivalent to a validated\ndeployment description. The topology and trajectories are propagated to the\ncontrol layer.\n\nThen, the system extracts from the description the network slice specification\nand any signal degradation models defined during the modeling process. With\nthese, it produces an in-memory Network Conceptual Graph (NCG), which contains\nthe aforementioned information and will be used by the system for the runtime\nstate propagation during the experimentation. The graph nodes represent\nnetwork and compute devices annotated with information about their\ncapabilities and deployed services, while edges denote the links between the\nnodes. The weight of each edge is determined by network QoS, incl. data rate,\nnetwork delay, packet and error rate. Then 5G-Slicer translates the NCG to an\nemulated environment by utilizing the Fogify Emulator Connector.\n\nThe connector is responsible for the emulation environment instantiation, and\nthe deployment of the IoT application through the FogifySDK. Furthermore, the\nTrajectory Manager parses the traces and applies the updates on the NCG, and,\nin turn propagates these to the running emulated environment. One can view\nthrough an interactive map the traces of mobile nodes, their performance (i.e.\ncpu, energy), and the load imposed to MECs.\n\n## Features\n\n### 5G Slicing Modeling\n\n5G-Slicer offers high-level modeling abstractions that capture the key\ncharacteristics of a 5G network slice along with the mobility of network\nentities. The model\'s expressivity enables users to design and build complex\n5G network slices, encapsulating QoS definition, user-plane network functions,\nphysical components, such as access points and base stations, physical nodes\'\npositioning and trajectories, new network technologies (multi-user MIMO and\nbeam-forming), and virtualized MEC and Cloud resources.\n\n### Positioning & Mobility\n\n5G-Slicer seamlessly "translates" the high-level 5G slicing description to a\nrunning emulated environment. At runtime, 5G-Slicer alters the positions of\nthe mobile entities based on the described trajectories, and, consequently,\nbased on entities\' positioning, alters at runtime the respective network QoS\nlink quality, such as network latency, bandwidth, error rate, etc.\n\n### ITS Use case template\n\n5G-Slicer provides a "ready-to-use" template for a city-scale transportation\nsector that users are able to introduce their services. Specifically, users\nsimply introduce the smart bus network testbed via the template that utilizes\nreal-world mobility data from the Dublin smart city project. In this, buses\ncontinuously report their locations and other attributes (i.e., environment\nconditions) to a central ITS to perform location-based analytic tasks (i.e.,\nbus delay reporting), in collaboration with employed MECs that act as local\ndata aggregators and are placed nearby bus stops.\n\n### Monitoring Capabilities\n\n5G-Slicer provides a wide-range of monitoring utilization metrics that\ncaptured from the deployed 5G-enabled application, such as CPU utilization,\noccupied memory size, network and disk I/O traffic. Moreover, users can\nextract application-level metrics to the emulator. Finally, the system\nintroduced new monitoring capabilities for packet-level monitoring and\nanalytics to the emulation suite.\n\n## Documentation\n\nYou will find the full documentation of the Fogify at the documentation page.\nAt Fogify\'s documentation, we provide details about installation, modeling,\nexperimentation, and, generally, a full get-started guide about the project.\n\n## Publications\n\nFor more details about 5G-Slicer and our scientific contributions, you can\nread the papers of 5G-Slicer and a published Demo. If you would like to use\n5G-Slicer for your research, you should include at least on of the following\nBibTeX entries.\n\n5G-Slicer\'s paper BibTeX citation:\n\n    \n    \n    @INPROCEEDINGS{Symeonides2022,\n    author    = {Symeonides, Moysis and Trihinas, Demetris and Pallis, George and Dikaiakos, Marios D. and Psomas, Constantinos and Krikidis, Ioannis},\n    title     = {5G-Slicer: An emulator for mobile IoT applications deployed over 5G network slices}, \n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 7th ACM/IEEE Conference on Internet of Things Design and Implementation},\n    year      = {2022}\n    series    = {IoTDI ’22}\n    }\n    \n\n5G-Slicer\'s demo BibTeX citation:\n\n    \n    \n    @INPROCEEDINGS{Symeonides2022,\n    author    = {Symeonides, Moysis and Trihinas, Demetris and Pallis, George and Dikaiakos, Marios D.},\n    title     = {Demo: Emulating 5G-Ready Mobile IoT Services},\n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 7th ACM/IEEE Conference on Internet of Things Design and Implementation}, \n    year      = {2022}\n    series    = {IoTDI ’22}\n    } \n    \n\n## Acknowledgements\n\nThis work is partially supported by the EU Commission through RAINBOW 871403\n(ICT-15-2019-2020) project and by the Cyprus Research and Innovation\nFoundation through COMPLEMENTARY/0916/0916/0171 and INFRASTRUCTURES/1216/0017\n(IRIDA) projects. Fogify provides a toolset to: model complex\nfog topologies comprised of heterogeneous resources, network capabilities and\nQoS criteria; deploy the modelled configuration and services using popular\ncontainerized infrastructure-as-code descriptions to a cloud or local\nenvironment; experiment, measure and evaluate the deployment by injecting\nfaults and adapting the configuration at runtime to test different "what-if"\nscenarios that reveal the limitations of a service before introduced to the\npublic.\n\n### Topology Editing\n\nA typical workflow starts with the user editing the docker-compose file of an\nIoT application, and extend it to encapsulate Fogify\'s model. The Fogify model\nis composed of: (i) _Fog Templates_ , allowing the description of _Services_ ,\n_Nodes_ and _Networks_ ; and (ii) the _Fog Topology_ , enabling users to\nspecify _Blueprints_. A Blueprint represents an emulated device and is a\ncombination of a _Node_ , _Service_ , _Networks_ , _replicas_ and a _label_.\nServices are inherited from docker-compose while the _x-fogify_ section\nprovides all Fogify primitives. Thus, users still develop their application\nusing familiar docker constructs with the added functionality of Fogify not\naffecting portability. This means that a Fogify enhanced description will run\nin any docker runtime environment without any alterations, however users will\nlose the functionality offered by Fogify.\n\n### Deployment\n\nWhen the description is ready, the user deploys the application using the\nFogifySDK through a Jupyter notebook, with the description received by the\nFogify Controller. If no error is detected by the Controller, it spawns the\nemulated devices and creates the overlay mesh networks between them,\ninstantiates the services, and broadcasts (any) network constraints to Fogify\nAgents. Specifically, the Controller translates the model specification to\nunderlying orchestration primitives and deploys them via the Cluster\nOrchestrator, ensuring the instantiation of the containerized services on the\nemulated environment. Located on every cluster node, Fogify Agents expose an\nAPI to accept requests from the Controller, apply network QoS primitives, and\nmonitor the emulated devices.\n\n### Testing\n\nOn a running emulated deployment, Fogify enables developers to apply _Actions_\nand "what-if" _Scenarios_ (sequences of timestamped actions) on their IoT\nservices, such as ad-hoc faults and topology changes. Actions and Scenarios\nare written by following the Fogify _Runtime Evaluation Model_. When an action\nor a scenario is submitted, the Fogify Controller coordinates its execution\nwith the Cluster Orchestrator and the respective Fogify Agents. Furthermore,\nFogify captures performance and app-level metrics via the Fogify Agent\nmonitoring module. All metrics are stored at the Agent\'s local storage and can\nbe retrieved from the FogifySDK.\n\n### Analysis\n\nTo create an end-to-end interactive analytic tool for emulated deployments, we\nexploit the FogifySDK capabilities in Jupyter Notebook stack. Specifically, we\npre-installed the FogifySDK library on Jupyter thus the user can (un-) deploy\na Fog Topology, apply ad-hoc changes and scenarios, and, especially, retrieve\nruntime performance metrics. For the latter, FogifySDK stores metrics to an\nin-memory data structure, namely panda\'s dataframe, providing exploratory\nanalysis methods that produce plots and summary statistics. Except of out-of-\nthe-box plots, provided by Pandas, we extended FogifySDK with tailored\nfunctions that provide a set of plots illustrating and explaining the effects\nof actions and scenarios in application performance. With the wide range of\nanalytic methods provided by FogifySDK, users extract useful insights about\nQoS, cost, and predictive analytics. Finally, users may integrate other\nlibraries, like scikit-learn, to endrose their analysis with ML and AI models.\n\n## Resources\n\n### Documentation\n\nYou will find the full documentation of the Fogify at the documentation page.\nAt Fogify\'s documentation, we provide details about installation, modeling,\nexperimentation, and, generally, a full get-started guide about the project.\n\n### The Team\n\nThe creators of the Fogify are members of the Laboratory for Internet\nComputing (LInC), University of Cyprus. You can find more information about\nour research activity visit our publications\' page and our on-going projects.\n\n### Publications\n\nFor more details about Fogify and our scientific contributions, you can read\nthe papers of Fogify and a published Demo. If you would like to use Fogify for\nyour research, you should include at least on of the following BibTeX entries.\n\nFogify\'s paper BibTeX citation:\n\n    \n    \n    @inproceedings{Symeonides2020,\n    author    = {Moysis, Symeonides and Zacharias, Georgiou and Demetris, Trihinas and George, Pallis and Marios D., Dikaiakos},\n    title     = {Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework},\n    year      = {2020},\n    publisher = {Association for Computing Machinery},\n    address   = {New York, NY, USA},\n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 5th ACM/IEEE Symposium on Edge Computing},\n    location  = {San Jose, CA, USA},\n    series    = {SEC ’20}\n    }\n    \n\nFogify\'s demo BibTeX citation:\n\n    \n    \n    @inproceedings{Symeonides2020,\n    author    = {Moysis, Symeonides and Zacharias, Georgiou and Demetris, Trihinas and George, Pallis and Marios D., Dikaiakos},\n    title     = {Demo: Emulating Geo-Distributed Fog Services},\n    year      = {2020},\n    publisher = {Association for Computing Machinery},\n    address   = {New York, NY, USA},\n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 5th ACM/IEEE Symposium on Edge Computing},\n    location  = {San Jose, CA, USA},\n    series    = {SEC ’20}\n    } \n    \n\n### Acknowledgements\n\nThis work is partially supported by the EU Commission through RAINBOW 871403\n(ICT-15-2019-2020) project and by the Cyprus Research and Innovation\nFoundation through COMPLEMENTARY/0916/0916/0171 project.\n\n### License\n\nThe framework is open-sourced under the Apache 2.0 License base. The codebase\nof the framework is maintained by the authors for academic research and is\ntherefore provided "as is".\n\n## About\n\nA Fog Computing Emulation Framework\n\n### Topics\n\njupyter  experimentation  fog-computing  edge-computing  fog-topology\n\n### Resources\n\nReadme\n\n### License\n\nApache-2.0 license\n\nActivity\n\n### Stars\n\n**24** stars\n\n### Watchers\n\n**8** watching\n\n### Forks\n\n**7** forks\n\nReport repository\n\n## Languages\n\n  * SCSS 49.8%\n  * Python 35.9%\n  * JavaScript 9.9%\n  * HTML 3.7%\n  * Other 0.7%\n\n## Footer\n\n(C) 2023 GitHub, Inc.\n\n### Footer navigation\n\n  * Terms\n  * Privacy\n  * Security\n  * Status\n  * Docs\n  * Contact GitHub\n  * Pricing\n  * API\n  * Training\n  * Blog\n  * About\n\nYou can’t perform that action at this time.\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://github.com/UCY-LINC-LAB/fogify', 'title': 'GitHub - UCY-LINC-LAB/fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework', 'description': 'A Fog Computing Emulation Framework. [Document(page_content="Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Installation Modes\n  * Requirement Software Components\n    * Orchestrator (Swarm Installation)\n    * Kernel Network Plugin\n  * Required Parameters\n\n# Installation\n\n## Installation Modes\n\nFogify can be installed either directly on cluster nodes, aka as a bare-metal\ninstallation, or the user can utilize a containerized version of the system\nwritten in docker-compose file. However, for both modes, the **all** cluster\nnodes should have installed the Requirement Software Components, namely, the\ndocker Swarm orchestrator and a network Linux kernel package (iproute).\n\n## Requirement Software Components\n\n### Orchestrator (Swarm Installation)\n\nAccording to the Orchestration, Fogify needs a pre-installed Docker Swarm\nOrchestrator. With the following command, the user can easily install a Docker\nSwarm Manager (master Node).\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    docker swarm init --advertise-addr <hosts_ip>\n    \n\nThe latter command will generate a result similar to:\n\n    \n    \n    Swarm initialized: current node (dxn1zf6l61qsb1josjja83ngz) is now a manager.\n    \n    To add a worker to this swarm, run the following command:\n    \n        docker swarm join \\\n        --token SWMTKN-1-49nj1cmql0jkz5s954yi3oex3nedyz0fb0xx14ie39trti4wxv-8vxv8rssmk743ojnwacrr2e7c \\\n        192.168.99.100:2377\n    \n    To add a manager to this swarm, run 'docker swarm join-token manager' and follow the instructions.\n    \n\nAt this time, the Docker Swarm cluster consists of one node which is Manager\nand Worker. If a user needs to add more nodes, he/she can run the following\ncommand on each extra node.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    \n    $ docker swarm join \\\n        --token SWMTKN-1-49nj1cmql0jkz5s954yi3oex3nedyz0fb0xx14ie39trti4wxv-8vxv8rssmk743ojnwacrr2e7c \\\n        192.168.99.100:2377\n        \n    \n\n### Kernel Network Plugin\n\nFogify executes some low-level commands in order to apply specific\ncharacteristics to the network. For this reason, on each cluster node, we\nshould install the traffic control tool (tc-tool). On Debian-based\ndestributions, tc-tool comes bundled with iproute, so in order to isntall it\nyou have to run:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    apt-get install iproute\n    \n\n## Required Parameters\n\nThe parameters of the `Fogify` should pass through host's environmental\nparameter. Specifically, the parameters are the following:\n\n  * `MANAGER_NAME`: the relative name of the swarm master node\n  * `MANAGER_IP`: the manager's IP\n  * `HOST_IP`: the machine's IP\n  * `CPU_OVERPROVISIONING_PERCENTAGE`: a CPU overprovisioning percentage, the default is `0`\n  * `RAM_OVERPROVISIONING_PERCENTAGE`: a CPU overprovisioning percentage, the default is `0`\n  * `CPU_FREQ`: The CPU frequency of the host machine\n\nA user selects a percentage of CPU or RAM overprovisioning, and Fogify will\ngenerate two limits: an upper limit and a lower limit for each emulated\ndevice. For instance, a 20% overprovissioning configuration demands the\nemulated nodes to occupy the 20% less than the maximum processing power that\nthe user selected. However, when any node requires extra power, the system\nwill provide it, if there are available resources. Generally, the system will\nprovide overprovisioning as a share competing portion of `CPU` or `RAM`.\n\nRunning `Fogify` through `docker-compose.yaml` the latter parameters may be\ndeclared in `.env` file or via command line parameters of `docker-compose up`\ncommand.\n\n#### Read more\n\n__Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework Fogify in Docker-compose __\n\n", metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/installation.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Installation | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  *     * Execution\n    * Docker-compose file\n\n# Fogify in Docker-compose\n\n### Execution\n\nTo ease the installation of Fogify, we created a docker-compose file that\ncontains a dockerized version of Fogify connected with a Jupyter server, which\nis used as a web-based GUI. Since, the Fogify and Jupyter stack is provided as\ndockerized services, we only need to run the following command at the swarm\nmaster node.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    sudo docker-compose -p fogemulator up\n    \n\nIn order to open the web interface of Jupyter, you have to find the output of\nthe `ui` service where the system outputs the `url` and the `token`\n\nFor instance, in previous output we can open the Jupyter interface with the\nfollowing url:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    http://127.0.0.1:8888/?token=1cd2e914cd03e76d551a666cb0a8dcdb6361bc29ddf54eed\n    \n\nIf we have more nodes in the cluster, we have to execute the following command\non every node.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    sudo docker-compose -p fogemulator up agent cadvisor\n    \n\nFor both modes, users should provide a set of parameters to compose file\n(written in .env file), specificaly:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    MANAGER_NAME=.... #The name of the swarm master node\n    MANAGER_IP=192.168.1.1 #The IP of the swarm master node\n    HOST_IP=192.168.1.1 #The IP of the host\n    CPU_OVERPROVISIONING_PERCENTAGE=... # A percentage of cpu over provisioning 0-100\n    RAM_OVERPROVISIONING_PERCENTAGE=... # A percentage of memory over provisioning 0-100 \n    CPU_FREQ= ... # The frequency of the underlying CPU \n    VERSION=.... #The version of Fogify\n    \n\n### Docker-compose file\n\nNext, we have the docker-compose file of Fogify system. The `fogify` and\n`fogify-jupyter` are images upload to docker-hub.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    version: \'3.7\'\n    \n    services:\n    \n      ui:\n        image: fogemulator/fogify-jupyter:${VERSION}\n        volumes:\n          - /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock\n          - /usr/bin/docker:/usr/bin/docker\n        ports:\n          - 8888:8888\n        environment:\n          - "JUPYTER_ENABLE_LAB=yes"\n          - "GRANT_SUDO=yes"\n        user: root\n      controller:\n        build: .\n        image: fogemulator/fogify:${VERSION} \n        entrypoint: [ "python", "/code/fogify/main.py", "--controller"]\n        volumes:\n          - /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock\n          - /usr/bin/docker:/usr/bin/docker\n        ports:\n          - 5000:5000\n        extra_hosts:\n          - ${MANAGER_NAME}:${MANAGER_IP}\n      agent:\n        image: fogemulator/fogify:${VERSION}\n        entrypoint: [ "python", "/code/fogify/main.py", "--agent", "--agent-ip", "${HOST_IP}"]\n        extra_hosts:\n          - ${MANAGER_NAME}:${MANAGER_IP}\n        volumes:\n          - /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock\n          - /usr/bin/docker:/usr/bin/docker\n          - /proc/:/proc/\n          - /var/run/docker/:/var/run/docker/\n          - /sys/class/net/:/sys/class/net/\n          - /usr/bin/nsenter:/usr/bin/nsenter\n          - /lib/modules:/lib/modules\n          - /sbin/modprobe:/sbin/modprobe\n        privileged: true\n        cap_add:\n          - ALL\n        depends_on:\n          - cadvisor\n          - controller\n        ports:\n          - 5500:5500\n        environment:\n          CONTROLLER_IP: ${MANAGER_IP}\n    \n      cadvisor:\n        image: gcr.io/google-containers/cadvisor:v0.35.0\n        volumes:\n          - /:/rootfs:ro\n          - /var/run:/var/run:ro\n          - /sys:/sys:ro\n          - /var/lib/docker/:/var/lib/docker:ro\n          - /dev/disk/:/dev/disk:ro\n        ports:\n          - 9090:8080\n        expose:\n          - 8080\n    \n\n#### Read more\n\n__Installation Bare-metal Installation __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/installation/as-a-service.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Fogify in Docker-compose | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  *     * Dependencies\n    * Fogify Controller (Master)\n    * Fogify Agent\n\n# Bare-metal Installation\n\n### Dependencies\n\nWhen we have installed the expected software components, now we have to\ninstall the main components of the Fogify System. Since Fogify is developed\nwith python, firstly, we install the python libraries with the following\ncommand (on each Cluster Node):\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    sudo pip3 install -r requirements.txt\n    \n\n### Fogify Controller (Master)\n\nThe Fogify Controller should run on the Cluster\'s Manager Node. The Controller\nwill receive any request and will communicate to the other nodes (Fogify\nAgents) in order to disseminate the appropriate commands.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n     python3  main.py --controller\n    \n\n### Fogify Agent\n\n#### Monitoring\n\nFor our initial version of Fogify, we utilize an external monitoring agent to\nendorse our monitoring metrics, namely the cAdvisor. Thus, when the Swarm\nCluster is up and running, the user should deploy the cAdvisor on each\nCluster\'s Node. The following command deploys a cAdvisor agent that exposes\nthe monitoring metrics to the 9090 port.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    #!/usr/bin/env bash\n    sudo docker run \\\n      --volume=/:/rootfs:ro \\\n      --volume=/var/run:/var/run:ro \\\n      --volume=/sys:/sys:ro \\\n      --volume=/var/lib/docker/:/var/lib/docker:ro \\\n      --volume=/dev/disk/:/dev/disk:ro \\\n      --publish=9090:8080 \\\n      --detach=true \\\n      --name=cadvisor \\\n      google/cadvisor:latest\n    \n\n#### Agent\'s Installation\n\nA Fogify Agent should run on each Swarm Node in order to apply the specific\nnetwork characteristics, retrieve the monitoring data and employ the stress\nactions. The agent should run with "sudo" because the network actions need\nadmins privileges.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    sudo python3  main.py --agent\n    \n\n#### Read more\n\n__Fogify in Docker-compose Getting started __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/installation/bare-metal.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Bare-metal Installation | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Prerequisites\n    * Jupyter GUI\n  * Step 1: Create the Application\n  * Step 2: Build the Dockerfile\n  * Step 3: Create the Compose file\n  * Step 4: Introduce the Fogify Model\n    * Nodes\n    * Networks\n    * Topology\n  * Step 5: Deploy the topology\n  * Step 6: Retrieve Metrics\n  * Step 7: Run an ad-hoc action\n  * Step 8: Build and run a Fogify Scenario\n  * Step 9: Representation of the Results\n  * Step 10: Undeploy the Topology\n\n# Getting started\n\nOn this page you build a simple Python micro-service IoT application that is\ndriven by real-world data to showcase a scenario of a taxi-cab company that\ncollects and analyzes location-based data from its fleet. The application\nincludes three services: a workload generator, an edge server and a cloud\nserver, all utilize the Flask framework. Even if the example is written in\nPython, the concepts demonstrated are understandable even if you’re not\nfamiliar with it.\n\n## Prerequisites\n\nBefore start the tutorial, make sure that already follow the installation\nguide of Fogify. You do not need to install anything else, such as python,\nsince it is provided as Docker image. If you are not familiar with docker, you\ncan find some information at the section of Services and at the Docker\nOfficial Documentation.\n\n### Jupyter GUI\n\nEven if Fogify exposes a REST API for interacting with the emulated testbed,\nit provides an extra python SDK with programming primitives. The FogifySDK\ngives us the opportunity to interconnect the Fogify with external systems like\nJupyter. The integration with Jupyter, as described in Fogify Docker-compose\ninstallation, provides a GUI for Fogify and an interactive way to work with\nit. Users can submit IoT service descriptions adopting the Fogify model\nspecification, manipulate service execution by applying actions and submitting\n"what-if" scenarios, extract real-time monitoring data and assess running\ndeployments. Furthermore, the Fogify SDK has a set of built-in analytics\nfunctions applicable on monitoring data, as well as, plotting functionality\nfor easing metric examination.\n\nNext image provides a snapshot of the Jupyter interface integrated with\nFogifySDK.\n\nUsers can use the editor provided by `Jupyter` to write the configuration yaml\nfiles, while interact with Fogify through the `Jupyter Notebooks`. We suggest\nthe use of `JupyterLab` as Jupyter GUI, since it provides many coding IDE\nfeatures that the developers are familiar with. For more information about how\ncan you reach the Jupyter Web GUI check the Fogify\'s Docker-compose\ninstallation guide.\n\nNext we describe step-by-step an application deployment on Fogify system.\n\n## Step 1: Create the Application\n\nSince the focus of this tutorial is not the coding, you will find the\ndemonstration code on github https://github.com/UCY-LINC-LAB/fogify-demo .\nSpecifically, you have only to download the repository and navigate to\n`application` folder and execute the `build-image.sh` script. The script\nbuilds the `Image` that we will describe in the following section.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ├── application\n    │\xa0\xa0 ├── build-image.sh\n    │\xa0\xa0 ├── docker-compose.yaml\n    │\xa0\xa0 └── taxi_exp\n    │\xa0\xa0     ├── code\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0 ├── collect_metrics.py\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0 ├── cronjobs\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0 ├── edge_server.py\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0 ├── entrypoint.sh\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0 ├── __init__.py\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0 ├── send_metrics_to_server.py\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0 ├── server.py\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0 └── utils\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0     ├── edge_fuctionality.py\n    │\xa0\xa0     │\xa0\xa0     └── __init__.py\n    │\xa0\xa0     ├── Dockerfile\n    │\xa0\xa0     └── requirements.txt\n    \n\n## Step 2: Build the Dockerfile\n\nThe repository provides the following `Dockerfile`, however, it is reasonable\nto describe it. The first line describes that `dockerfile` is based on\n`python:3.6`. Next, it install a set of tools that is required from Fogify\n(`cpulimit` and `stress` tools). At the next step, `Dockerfile` introduces the\nexample\'s code and configures the `cron` jobs (essential for this example).\nFinally, `Dockerfile` configures the `entrypoint` of the image. For more\ninformation about `dockerfiles`, you can read the docker\'s official\ndocumentation about `dockerfiles`.\n\nIf the `cpulimit` and `stress` are not installed on the docker image, Fogify\nwill only not provide `stress` actions. However, the rest Fogify\nfunctionalities will be provided and not effect Fogify\'s execution.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    # Pull base image of Python\n    FROM python:3.6\n    \n    # Set environment variables\n    ENV PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE 1\n    ENV PYTHONUNBUFFERED 1\n    \n    # Install the cpu-limit and stress tool pre-requirements for fully functional Fogify\n    RUN git clone https://github.com/opsengine/cpulimit/\n    WORKDIR cpulimit\n    RUN make && cp src/cpulimit /usr/bin\n    RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y stress && apt-get -y install cron rsyslog\n    \n    # Add the python code\n    RUN mkdir /code\n    WORKDIR /code\n    ADD requirements.txt /code/\n    RUN pip install -r requirements.txt\n    \n    EXPOSE 8000\n    \n    ADD ./code/ /code/\n    \n    # Install cron tab\n    RUN chmod 0644 /code/cronjobs\n    RUN echo "cron.* /var/log/cron.log" >> /etc/rsyslog.conf\n    RUN service rsyslog start\n    \n    # Insert and execute entrypoint\n    RUN chmod +x /code/entrypoint.sh\n    CMD ["/bin/bash", "/code/entrypoint.sh"]\n    \n\n## Step 3: Create the Compose file\n\nThis is the initial docker-compose file of the project. This file includes\nfour services, namely, `cloud-server`, `mec-svc-1`, `mec-svc-2`, `car-\nworkload`. Each service executes a different part of code, specifically:\n\n  * **cloud-server** : gathers the results of all MECs and stores them\n  * **mec-svc-1 & mec-svc-2**: should be deployed on different regions, capture the regional data and preprocess them\n  * **car-workload** : this service generates the streams of regional data\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    version: \'3.7\'\n    services:\n      cloud-server:\n        image: taxi-exp:0.0.1\n        environment:\n          NODE_TYPE: CLOUD_NODE\n      car-workload:\n        image: taxi-exp:0.0.1\n        environment:\n          NODE_TYPE: IOT_NODE\n        volumes:\n          - /home/ubuntu/data:/data\n      mec-svc-1:\n        image: taxi-exp:0.0.1\n        environment:\n          NODE_TYPE: EDGE_NODE\n          REGION: bronx\n      mec-svc-2:\n        image: taxi-exp:0.0.1\n        environment:\n          NODE_TYPE: EDGE_NODE\n          REGION: brooklyn\n    \n\n## Step 4: Introduce the Fogify Model\n\nWhen the `docker-compose` is ready, user can extend it to capture the extra\nfeatures of the Fogify Framework. The following part of the extend `docker-\ncompose` yaml file illustrates three required components of the model:\n`nodes`, `networks` and `topology`.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ...\n    \n    x-fogify:\n        nodes:\n            ...\n        networks:\n            ...\n        topology:\n            ...\n    \n\n### Nodes\n\n`Nodes` template is used to define Fog resources. In our scenario we have 3\ndifferent types of nodes (`car-node`, `cloud-server-node`, and `edge-node`).\nThe `Node` template allows users to describe the resource characteristics of a\nphysical or virtual host, including properties for the `Processor`, `Memory`,\nand `Storage`.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n      nodes:\n        - name: cloud-server-node\n          capabilities:\n            processor:\n              cores: 4\n              clock_speed: 1400\n            memory: 4G\n        - name: edge-node\n          capabilities:\n            processor:\n              cores: 2\n              clock_speed: 1400\n            memory: 2G\n        - name: car-node\n          capabilities:\n            processor:\n              cores: 1\n              clock_speed: 700\n            memory: 0.5G\n    \n\nFor more details about nodes you can visit the node profile documentation\npage.\n\n### Networks\n\n`Networks` template is used to define inter-connecting mesh networks and links\namong Fog nodes. Fog nodes can be directly connected via an emulated physical\nlink and/or belong to the same network administrative domain. Furthermore,\nnetwork template provides a wide variety of properties like `bandwidth`,\n`network delay`, `drop rate`, etc. The following networks sub-section\ndescribes the networks that exist at our example. Starting from the `internet`\nnetwork definition, we can identify different network characteristics for\nuplink and downlink properties. Furthermore, we described two extra regional\nnetworks, namely `edge-net-1` and `edge-net-2` that only characterized by\n`bidirectional` characteristics. The `bidirectional` property defines the same\nnetwork characteristics for both `uplink` and `downlink` directions.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n      networks:\n        - name: internet\n          uplink:\n            bandwidth: 10Mbps\n            latency:\n              delay: 50ms\n            drop: 0.1%\n          downlink:\n            bandwidth: 5Mbps\n            latency:\n              delay: 50ms\n        - name: edge-net-1\n          bidirectional:\n            bandwidth: 100Mbps\n            latency:\n              delay: 5ms\n            drop: 0.1%\n        - name: edge-net-2\n          bidirectional:\n            bandwidth: 100Mbps\n            latency:\n              delay: 5ms\n            drop: 0.1%\n    \n\nFor more details about networks you can visit the network profile\ndocumentation page.\n\n### Topology\n\n`Services`, `Nodes` and `Networks` only describe the provisioning of services\nand resources, lacking information on how a fog topology is realised and\ninterconnected and where services are placed. So, Fogify provides the\n`Topology` primitive, enabling users to specify a set of `Blueprints`, which\nis a combination of a `Node`, `Service`, set of `Networks`, `replicas` and a\n`label`.\n\nFor instance, the `Blueprint` of the following code part materializes two\nvehicles (`replicas: 2`) that are connected to the `mec-net-1` and `internet`\nnetworks, and run the `car-workload` service.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n        - node: car-node\n          service: car-workload\n          label: car-workload-1\n          replicas: 2\n          networks:\n            - edge-net-1\n            - internet\n    \n\nSimilarly, the user describes all components from the application scenario\nillustrated as are depicted on the following code snippet. The combination of\nservices, nodes and templates allows users to create more complex topologies.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n      topology:\n        - node: cloud-server-node\n          service: cloud-server\n          label: cloud-server\n          replicas: 1\n          networks:\n            - internet\n        - node: edge-node\n          service: mec-svc-1\n          label: mec-svc-1\n          replicas: 1\n          networks:\n            - edge-net-1\n            - internet\n        - node: edge-node\n          service: mec-svc-2\n          label: mec-svc-2\n          replicas: 1\n          networks:\n            - edge-net-2\n            - internet\n        - node: car-node\n          service: car-workload\n          label: car-workload-1\n          replicas: 2\n          networks:\n            - edge-net-1\n            - internet\n        - node: car-node\n          service: car-workload\n          label: car-workload-2\n          replicas: 2\n          networks:\n            - edge-net-2\n            - internet\n    \n\nFor more details about topologies and blueprints you can visit the\ndocumentation page.\n\n## Step 5: Deploy the topology\n\nEven if users can use a RESTful API to deploy topologies on Fogify, the\neasiest way is by utilizing the FogifySDK (integrated with Jupyter). The\nfollowing lines of code illustrate the use of FogifySDK. Specifically, the\nuser imports the SDK, instantiates a fogify object that includes information\nabout the controller\'s url and the topology description file, and, finally,\nexecutes the `deploy` function that submits the topology to the fogify\'s\nController.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    from FogifySDK import FogifySDK\n    fogify = FogifySDK("http://controller:5000","docker-compose.yaml")\n    \n    fogify.deploy()\n    \n\nWhile the Fogify is trying to deploy the topology, system displays a progress\nbar.\n\nAt the end, when the deployment is over, the system generates a simple message\nto the end-users.\n\n## Step 6: Retrieve Metrics\n\nIn order to retrieve the monitoring metrics from a specific service, users can\njust execute the following command.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.get_metrics_from(\'mec-svc-1.1\')\n    \n\nEspecially, users only need to determine the service\'s `label` along with the\ninstance\'s number. For instance, the service\'s label at the following example\nis the `mec-svc-1` and the instance number is the `1`. The results of the\nabove command will produce the following table on Jupyter Notebook.\n\nThe above table is a `pandas` dataframe, so, users can generate a wide rage of\nplots from it. For instance, a user can generate the plot of CPU utilization\nby executing the following command.\n\n## Step 7: Run an ad-hoc action\n\nFogify gives users the opportunity to execute ad-hoc actions (see Actions &\nScenarios section). The possible actions include `horizontal scaling`,\n`vertical scaling`, `network changes`, `stressing of resources`, and direct\n`commands` on emulated nodes. The following code snippet displays an example\nof the action\'s execution. Specifically, on the previous running topology we\ninjected a `stress` action that fires a `70%` cpu intensive workload in `mec-\nsvc-1.1` instance.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    \n    fogify.stress(\'mec-svc-1\', cpu=70)\n    \n\nIn order to observe if the action has the desirable effects, we retrieve again\nthe metrics of the instance and plot the cpu utilization. As you can see on\nthe following image, the effect took place for one minute between 65-75\nintervals.\n\n## Step 8: Build and run a Fogify Scenario\n\nWith actions tested, let us introduce the `Scenarios`, which is a sequence of\ntime-based actions. Following we describe a scenario that degrades the network\nconnectivity of `mec-svc-1`. Specifically, after 5 seconds from the scenario\nbeginning the network connectivity of `mec-svc-1` degrades with a network\nlatency up to 50ms per request. Similarly, after 15 seconds the network get\nworse with 150ms and, finally, after 5 seconds the network delay reach 3000ms\nper request.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    \n        scenarios:\n        - name: scenario_network_error\n          actions: \n            - time: 20\n              instance_type: car-1\n              instances: 1\n              position: 0\n              action:\n                type: network\n                parameters:\n                    network: MEC-net-1\n                    uplink:\n                        latency:\n                          delay: 50ms\n            - time: 20\n              instance_type: car-1\n              instances: 1\n              position: 1\n              action:\n                type: network\n                parameters:\n                    network: MEC-net-1\n                    uplink:\n                        latency:\n                          delay: 150ms\n            - time: 0\n              instance_type: car-2\n              instances: 1\n              position: 2\n              action:\n                type: scale-in\n                parameters:\n                  num-of-instances: 1\n                  \n    \n\nIn order to execute the scenario, FogifySDK provides the `scenario_execution`\nfunction that submits a scenario to Fogify. Next snippet of code executes a\npipeline of actions. Especially, user submits the scenario and, then, Fogify\nexecutes the scenario by executing one-by-one all the actions. Furthermore,\nFogify displays a progress bar of the scenario execution.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    start, end = fogify.scenario_execution(\'scenario_1\')\n    \n\nNext, we demonstrate the results of the previous code execution.\n\n## Step 9: Representation of the Results\n\nIn order to have an overview about the scenario\'s execution, Fogify gives to\nthe users specific methods of results representation. For instance, after the\nprevious scenario\'s execution, the user retrieves the generated data by\nfiltering by scenario\'s time-range. Furthermore, Fogify provides the timestamp\nof the events and user is able to combine them. In the following code part,\nuser retrieves the data of mec-svc-1 service, generates the edge network-out\nand network-in timelines, and, also, depicts the timestamp ( vertical lines )\nof the scenario\'s actions.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    \n    import matplotlib.pyplot as plt\n    import pandas as pd\n    fig, ax = plt.subplots()\n    \n    data = fogify.get_metrics_from(\'mec-svc-1.1\')\n    data = data[data.index>start]\n    data = data[data.index<end]\n    \n    data[\'network_tx_edge-net-1\'].diff().plot(ax=ax,label="network-out")\n    data[\'network_rx_edge-net-1\'].diff().plot(ax=ax,label="network-in")\n    ax.legend()\n    fogify.plot_annotations(ax, start=start, stop=end, colors_gist=[\'gray\',\'darkgray\', \'gray\', \'black\'])\n    \n\nThe results of the previous lines are illustrated on the following image:\n\n## Step 10: Undeploy the Topology\n\nFinally, the user undeploys the emulated infrastructure by executing the\n`undeploy` method.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.undeploy()\n    \n\nThe Fogify provides a process bar during the undeployment process. When all\ninstances are destroyed, system visualizes a representative message.\n\n#### Read more\n\n__Bare-metal Installation Services __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/getting-started.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Getting started | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Preliminaries\n    * Dockerfiles\n    * Images\n    * Containers\n  * Docker-compose files\n\n# Services\n\nServices are self-contained binaries, made up of libraries, tools, and\ndependencies for the codebase. The services should be described with exactly\nthe same way as docker-compose specification.\n\n## Preliminaries\n\nDocker provides a standardized way for building, sharing and executing\ncontainerized applications. Specifically, `dockerfiles` are files that include\nall details for building docker `Images`. `Images` package all the service\'s\ncode, dependencies, artifacts, etc. The system stores `images` on local or\nremote repositories. The most well-known publicly available repository is\ndocker-hub. `Docker containers` are the running instances of the images and,\nconsequently, the execution environment of Fog Node emulated instances.\n\n### Dockerfiles\n\nAs we explained before, Docker builds images automatically by scanning the\ninstructions from a Dockerfile. A Dockerfile is a file that includes all\ninstructions that the user calls in order to assemble a docker image. To build\na new docker image, users run the build command that executes the\ninstructions, creates and stores the new image. A simple example of a\ndockerfile is the following:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    FROM ubuntu:18.04\n    COPY . /app\n    RUN make /app\n    CMD python /app/app.py\n    \n\nFor more example and a detail documentation, we suggest the dockerfile\'s\nofficial documentation.\n\n### Images\n\nThe simplest way to create an image is to build a dockerfile. The `docker\nbuild` command creates a Docker image from a Dockerfile. We can use the `-t`\nflag in order to specify a tag for the created image. Usually, this tag is the\nname of the image along with its version. For instance the following command\ncreates an image with the `simple-app:0.1` tag, which illustrates that the\nimage contains the version `0.1` of the `simple-app` service.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    docker build -t simple-app:0.1 . \n    \n\nOne can search the available images on the local host by running the `docker\nimage ls` command.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    docker image ls\n    \n\nFor more example and a detail documentation, we suggest to check the available\ncommands like `image pull`, `image rm`, etc, on docker command documentation\nwhile dedicated pages exist for the docker image\'s docker image and docker\nbuild documentations.\n\nSimilarly to Docker Swarm, in a Fogify deployment, the images should be either\nregistered on every single node of the Fogify\'s Cluster or should be uploaded\non a publicly available repository.\n\n### Containers\n\nWhen a user "runs" an image, a running instance of that image is created,\nnamely a docker container. The `docker run` command execute a docker image and\ncreates a docker `container`. For instance the following command creates a\ndocker container from the `simple-app:0.1` image.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    docker run simple-app:0.1 \n    \n\nSimilarly with the other concepts of docker, there are many parameters and\ncommands that a user can use. Again, a more detailed view of docker\ncontainer\'s commands is provided on the docker\'s command line official\ndocumentation\n\n## Docker-compose files\n\n`Docker-compose` is a toolkit for determining and executing multi-container\napplications. A YAML file defines and configures the application\'s services.\nDocker-compose helps users to create, start, and stop all services. The\ndocker-compose specification configures many concepts that an application\nneeds, such as environmental parameters, dependencies between the services,\nresources from local host, exported container\'s ports, and many more. An\noverview of the docker-compose can be found on the official page. To\nillustrate the functionalities of docker-compose, followingly, we present an\nexample of a typical docker-compose file (`docker-compose.yaml`) that\ndescribes an `Apache Storm` cluster:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    services:  # The list of the available services\n      zookeeper:  # The service name that we use as service identifier\n        image: zookeeper  # The image of the service\n        restart: always\n      nimbus:  \n        image: storm:2.1.0 \n        command: storm nimbus\n        depends_on:  \n          - zookeeper  # This determines that the service nimbus will wait until the zookeeper starts\n        restart: always\n        ports: # On this port the service receives external requests (host-port:container-port)\n          - 6627:6627 \n        volumes: # We can pass specific files into the service file system (host-path:container-path)\n           - /home/TestTopology.jar:/example/TestTopology.jar  \n      ui:\n        image: storm:2.1.0\n        command: storm ui\n        depends_on:\n          - nimbus\n          - zookeeper\n        restart: always\n        ports:\n          - 8080:8080\n      supervisor:\n        image: storm:2.1.0\n        command: storm supervisor\n        depends_on:\n          - nimbus\n          - zookeeper\n        restart: always\n    \n\n#### Read more\n\n__Getting started Node Profiles __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/services.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Services | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content="Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin's Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Description\n  * Parameters\n    * Name\n    * Capabilities\n\n# Node Profiles\n\n## Description\n\nThe `Nodes` section is used to define Fog resources. A fog infrastructure is\ncomposed of machines with various resource capabilities from low processing\npower machines, like Raspberries, to public cloud VMs, like Amazon's EC2. To\ncapture this heterogeneity `Nodes` section allows users to describe the\nresource characteristics of a physical or virtual host, including properties\nfor the `Processor`, `Memory`, and `Storage`.  \nUsers can determine multiple different Node profiles, which can be used in\nmultiple Fog instances at the instantiation phase.\n\nFollowing, we demonstrate how a raspberry pi 3b can be described:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    nodes:\n    - name: raspberry_pi_3_B\n      capabilities:\n        processor:\n          cores: 4\n          clock_speed: 1400\n        memory: 1G\n        disk: \n            type: SDcard\n            size: 8G\n            read: 95MB/s\n            write: 90MB/s\n    \n\n## Parameters\n\n### Name\n\n`Name` is the identifier of the node profile. Users use `name` to specify\nwhich fog node has the specific node capabilities.\n\n### Capabilities\n\n#### Processor\n\n`Processor` characterizes the CPU capabilities of the current node profile.\nSpecifically, users defines the `cores` that is the number of CPU's cores and\nthe `clock_speed` that is the CPU frequency. By default, the units of\n`clock_speed` is the megahertz and the user should not define them. After the\ndeployment, Fogify translates the latter into the `cgroup` constraints,\ndedicated for each running container.\n\n#### Memory\n\nSimilarly with processor tag, `memory` specifies the amount of RAM that a Fog\nnode is equipped with. The available units of memory property is `G` for\ngigabyte and `M` for megabyte.\n\n#### Disk\n\n`Disk` defines the node's characteristics related to storage properties. With\n`disk` users can set the `type` of storage device (possible values are:\n`SDcard`, `SSD`, `HDD`), its `size` of storage in gigabyte (`G`) or megabyte\n(`M`), `read` and `write` speed in `MB/S`.\n\nIn current version of Fogify, `disk` properties do not effect the deployment.\nWe are working on that feature and we will provide it in near future.\n\n#### Read more\n\n__Services Network QoS and VNFs __\n\n", metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/node-profiles.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Node Profiles | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Description\n  * Parameters\n    * Name\n    * Uplink & Downlink\n    * Network Latency\n    * Capacity\n    * Packet Level Monitoring\n    * Firewall Rules\n    * Links\n\n# Network QoS and VNFs\n\n## Description\n\nWe consider that an application spans on different nodes and sites through one\nor more network connections. There could be significant heterogeneity in the\nupward and downward links due to widely different link capacities. In our\nmodel, one specifies multiple parameters for network connectivity like delay,\npacket loss rate, packet corruption, etc.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n        networks:\n        - name: internet\n          uplink:\n            bandwidth: 10Mbps\n            latency:\n              delay: 20ms\n            drop: 0.01%\n          downlink:\n            bandwidth: 10Mbps\n            latency:\n              delay: 20ms\n            drop: 0.01%\n          packet_level_monitoring: \'TRUE\'  # optional property\n          firewall_rules:  # optional property\n            - protocol: TCP # optional property\n              from_port: 80 # optional property\n              to_port: 8080 # optional property\n              type: DROP # optional property\n              from: fog-node-label-1 # optional property\n              to: fog-node-label-2 # optional property\n    \n\n## Parameters\n\n### Name\n\n`Name` is the identifier of the network profile. Users use `name` to specify\nwhich fog node is connected to specific networks.\n\n### Uplink & Downlink\n\nFogify provides users the ability to define different `uplink` and `downlink`\ncharacteristics. Specifically, users can define network `latency`, `bandwidth`\nand `drop` packet rate. We should note here that if a user would like to\ndetermine a general characteristic between two nodes, user has to specify both\n`uplink` and `downlink`. For instance, if the network delay between two nodes,\nA and B, is `6ms` user should determine `3ms` uplink and `3ms` downlink in\nboth nodes. The measurement unit of `bandwidth` is `Mbps` while the `drop`\nrate is determined by a percentage (e.g. `0.1%`). The next subsection\nillustrates the network `latency` definition since it can be much more complex\nthan `bandwidth` or `drop` rate.\n\n### Network Latency\n\n`Latency` is composed of the average network `delay` and the optional\nproperties of `deviation`, which is the deviation between the mean and the\nmax/min values of the delay, and the `correlation`, which determines the\nmaximum percent of difference between previous delay value and the current\none. Both `delay` and `deviation` are measured in `ms`. Finally, users can\ndetermine the `distribution` of the delay\'s values. The by-default available\ndistributions are `uniform`, `gaussian`, `pareto` and `paretonormal`, however,\nusers can upload their own ping delay traces and the system generates any\ncustom distribution.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ...\n            latency:\n              delay: 20ms\n              deviation: 5ms\n              correlation: 20%\n              distribution: uniform\n    ...\n    \n\n### Capacity\n\n`Capacity` restricts the number of connected devices on a network.\n\nIn current version of Fogify, `Capacity` does not effect the deployment. We\nare working on that feature and we will provide it in near future.\n\n### Packet Level Monitoring\n\nPacket level monitoring enables the monitoring and analysis of network\'s\npackets statistics. The default value of `packet_level_monitoring` is `FALSE`,\nsince this procedure is too compute intensive. If the users need to inspect\nthe packet traffic should set `packet_level_monitoring` to `TRUE`.\n\n### Firewall Rules\n\nUsers can attach firewall rules to a network through `firewall_rules` field.\nSpecifically, a firewall rule object includes the connection `protocol`\n(`TCP`, `UDP`), `type` (`DROP`, `ACCEPT`, `REDIRECT`), source port\n(`from_port`) & destination port (`to_port`), and source fog node (`from`) &\ndestination fog node (`to`). All fields are optional, but a firewall rule\nobject should have at least one. At a low level, Fogify utilizes the Linux\niptables tool that allows the system to apply the IP packet filter rules of\nthe Linux kernel firewall, implemented as different Netfilter modules.\n\n### Links\n\nWith `links` users are able to define specific characteristics on top of\npackets that transfer between pears of emulated nodes. The definition of a\n`link`, user should define the `from_node` property that determines the source\nof the packets, `to_node` property that specifies the destination of the\npackets, and the `properties`, which are the similar as the network\nproperties. A boolean optional field, named `bidirectional`, determines if a\nsimilar rule will be applied to the `from_node` to `to_node` link.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ...\n        networks:\n        - name: internet\n          uplink:\n            bandwidth: 10Mbps\n            latency:\n              delay: 20ms\n            drop: 0.01%\n          downlink:\n            bandwidth: 10Mbps\n            latency:\n              delay: 20ms\n            drop: 0.01%\n          links:\n            from_node: "cloud-server"\n            to_node: "mec-svc-1"\n            bidirectional: true\n            properties:\n                latency:\n                  delay: 200ms\n    ...\n    \n\nThe latter example illustrates a bidirectional link between `cloud-server`\nnode and `mec-svc-1` node is `200ms`.\n\n#### Read more\n\n__Node Profiles Blueprints __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/network-qos.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Network QoS and VNFs | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content="Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin's Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Description\n  * Parameters\n    * Label\n    * Service\n    * Node\n    * Replicas\n    * Networks\n\n# Blueprints\n\n## Description\n\n`Topology` element is a combination of a `node`, a `service`, attached\n`networks` and a replication factor (`replicas`). Finally, each node has a\n`label` which represents the name of the node at the deployed dockerized\napplication. In the following example we have three `node-sm` nodes connected\nto the `internet` network (with specific connectivity characteristics) that\nwill execute the `nimbus` and `supervisor` services respectively.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n        topology:\n            - node: node-sm  # Node template as described in Node profiles\n              service: nimbus  # Service as described in docker-compose services\n              label: nimbus  # label/identifier of the emulated fog node \n              replicas: 1  # replication factor of the node\n              networks:  # a list of the networks that the node is connected to\n                - internet\n            - node: node-sm\n              service: supervisor\n              label: supervisor\n              replicas: 2\n              networks:\n                - internet\n    \n\n## Parameters\n\n### Label\n\n`Label` is the identifier of the `blueprint`. Users can use the `label` to\nspecify the instances for injecting `actions` and `scenarios`. Furthermore,\nusers can include a number after the `label` to identify specific replica of\nthe blueprint, e.g `supervisor.1`.\n\n### Service\n\n`Service` is the executable that will run on the Fog node. The `service` is\ninherited from `services` section of the `docker-compose` specification. For\nmore details check out the following link.\n\n### Node\n\nSpecifies on which emulated device the service will run on. The emulated node\ninherits the `capabilities` of `node profile`. For more details check out the\nfollowing link.\n\n### Replicas\n\n`Replicas` identifies the number of instances that Fogify will create from the\nspecific `blueprint`. All instances will have the same processing\ncharacteristics, execute the same service and are connected on the same\nnetworks.\n\n### Networks\n\nThis section provides information about node networking. Specifically, users\nselect in which `networks` the `blueprint` will be connected. For instance, at\nthe before-mentioned example, `supervisor` nodes will be connected to the\n`internet` network with default network connectivity QoS. If there is a need\nfor node-specific network QoS, user can override them. Following example\nillustrates how do users override the network QoS.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ....\n            - node: node-sm\n              service: supervisor\n              label: supervisor\n              replicas: 2\n              networks:\n                - name: internet\n                  uplink:\n                    bandwidth: 1Mbps\n                    latency:\n                      delay: 200ms\n                    drop: 0.01%\n                  downlink:\n                    bandwidth: 1Mbps\n                    latency:\n                      delay: 200ms\n                    drop: 0.01%\n    ....\n    \n\nCurrently, user has to determine again all network properties again, even if\nthe desired properties are the same with default.\n\n#### Read more\n\n__Network QoS and VNFs Actions & Scenarios __\n\n", metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/blueprints.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Blueprints | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Actions\n    * Horizontal Scaling\n    * Vertical Scaling\n    * Network\n    * Stress\n    * Command\n  * Scenarios\n\n# Actions & Scenarios\n\nThe Fogify\'s model abstractions enable the rapid prototyping of emulated Fog\ndeployments. However, Fog deployments are usually neither statically\nprovisioned nor stable. This instability highly impacts the execution of IoT\nservices, especially in uncontrollable domains. Fogify addresses this\nchallenge by providing runtime `Actions` & `Scenarios`. `Action` is a process\nthat changes properties of a running Fog Topology while `Scenario` allows the\nrepeatable execution of a series of `Actions` written in a yaml format.\n\n## Actions\n\nThe user can execute various actions at runtime that can alter the underlying\ninfrastructure. To achieve that a user can execute `POST` call to\n`<manager>:5000/action/<action_type>` or can utilize the FogifySDK. For\n`action_type`, we have various types, namely: `horizontal_scaling`,\n`vertical_scaling`, `network`, `command` and `stress`.
