Users can determine\neither a `blueprint` `label` and the `number` of instances that the action\nwould like to affect or the label along with the number of a specific node,\ne.g. `supervisor.5`.\n\n### Horizontal Scaling\n\nFor horizontal scaling actions, we have to select the instance type (`label`),\nthe number of instances and the action that will be applied (`up` or `down`)\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    { \n      "params":{\n        "instance_type" : "supervisor-1", \n        "instances": 2, \n        "type":"up"\n        } \n    \n    }\n    \n\nCurrently, Fogify does not guarantee that the horizontal scaling action will\nbe apply, user has to be sure about the extra resources.\n\n### Vertical Scaling\n\nFor vertical scaling actions, we have to select the instance type (`label`),\nand the action that will be applied. For `CPU` power, user can define a cpu\npercent of increase (`+<percent>`) or decrease (`-<percent>`). For `memory`,\none defines the new memory limit. We can not define both cpu and memory\nvertical scaling at once.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    { \n      "params":{\n        "instance_type" : "supervisor-1.1", \n        "cpu":"+20",\n        "memory": "3G"\n        } \n    \n    }\n    \n\nCurrently, Fogify does not guarantee that the vertical scaling action will be\napply, user has to be sure about the extra resources.\n\n### Network\n\nThis action updates the network connectivity of a node. Again, the user\nselects the instance type (`label`) and the action object that contains\nvarious network parameter like `delay`, `bandwidth`, `drop` etc. Furthermore,\na user selects a specific network. At the following example, we apply our\naction to the `supervisor-1` to the `internet` network connection.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    { "params":{\n    \t"instance_type" : "supervisor-1", \n    \t"instances": 1, \n    \t"action":{\n    \t\t"uplink":{\n    \t\t\t"latency":{"delay":"100ms"}, \n    \t\t\t"bandwidth": "100Mbps", \n    \t\t\t"drop": 0.0001},\n    \t\t"downlink":{\n    \t\t\t"latency":{"delay":"100ms"}, \n    \t\t\t"bandwidth": "100Mbps", \n    \t\t\t"drop": 0.0001}, \n    \t"network":"internet"}} \n    \t}\n    \n\n### Stress\n\nFogify can inject extra workload to specific node(s) in order to simulate the\ninterferences of colocated service on a node. For instance, with the following\njson object, Fogify will inject a 50% cpu-intensive workload for 300s to one\ninstance of the node `supervisor-1`.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n        { \n        "params":{\n            "instance_type" : "supervisor-1", \n            "instances": 1, \n            "action":{\n                "cpu":50,\n                "duration": "300s"\n                }\t\n            } \n        }\n    \n\n### Command\n\nFogify can inject terminal command to specific node(s). The latter helps users\nto execute even user-defined actions on running fog nodes. For instance, with\nthe following json object, Fogify will inject a submission command on `nimbus`\nnode.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n        { \n        "params":{\n            "instance_type" : "nimbus", \n            "instances": 1, \n            "action":{\n                "command": "/bin/storm jar test.jar test-topology"\n                }\t\n            } \n        }\n    \n\n## Scenarios\n\nWith the Scenarios, a user will be able to define predefined series of actions\nat specific time. For instance, at the `scenario_1` the first action will be\nexecuted at 5th minute from the started point of the experiment.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    scenarios:\n    - name: scenario_1\n      actions: \n        - time: 30\n          position: 0\n          instance_type: supervisor-1\n          instances: 1\n          action:\n            type: network\n            parameters:\n                network: edge-net-1\n                bidirectional:\n                  bandwidth: 100Mbps\n                  drop: 0.1%\n                  latency:\n                    delay: 1000ms\n        - time: ....\n    \n\n#### Read more\n\n__Blueprints Monitoring __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/actions-and-scenarios.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Actions & Scenarios | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Default Metrics\n  * User-defined Metrics\n\n# Monitoring\n\nFogify provides a wide rage of monitoring metrics for each emulated instance\nand is able to extract user-defined metrics.\n\n## Default Metrics\n\nFogify captures performance metrics directly from the containerized process by\ninspecting the containers. Pre-defined metrics available by Fogify include CPU\ntime, memory usage, network traffic and many more. The following table depicts\nall available metrics provided by `Fogify`\n\nmetric | description  \n---|---  \ncpu | The accumulative CPU time occupied by an emulated instance  \ncpu_util | The average utilization of CPU between two measurements  \nmemory | The occupied memory by an emulated instance  \nmemory_util | The utilization of the emulated instance\'s memory  \nnetwork_rx_{network name} | The accumulative received bytes from a specific\nnetwork  \nnetwork_tx_{network name} | The accumulative transmitted bytes from a specific\nnetwork  \n  \n## User-defined Metrics\n\nUsers can expose application-level metrics for their IoT services. This is\nachieved by exposing metric updates, in JSON format, to a file\n(`fogify.metrics.json`) via the container root directory interface. Fogify\nwill then retrieve them via a lightweight monitoring probe. When the agent\nretrieves the data, it stores them to the monitoring storage. Following, we\noffer an exemplary `fogify.metrics.json` file.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    {\n      "response-time": 500,\n      "requests": 6530,\n      "log-in-requests": 100\n    }\n    \n\nIn the previous json file there are three metrics exposed by the application,\nnamely, the response time (`response-time`), requests count (`requests`) and\nlogin request count (`log-in-requests`).\n\nCurrently, the metric\'s name should be string and its value should be numeric.\n\n#### Read more\n\n__Actions & Scenarios Connection with third parties and API __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/monitoring.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Monitoring | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Fogify\'s Restfull API\n    * Deploy Topology\n    * Undeploy Topology\n    * Deploy Actions\n    * Get Monitoring Metrics\n    * Remove Monitoring Metrics\n  * Miscellaneous\n    * Deploy a Network Distribution\n  * Python SDK (FogifySDK)\n\n# Connection with third parties and API\n\n## Fogify\'s Restfull API\n\nThe Fogify Controller exposes a REST API for interacting with the emulated\ntestbed. Next we describe in details the available methods along with their\nparameters. Specifically, users can deploy and undeploy topologies, execute\nad-hoc actions and retrieve monitored metrics.\n\n### Deploy Topology\n\nThe user deploys his/her topology with a `POST` api call to the\n`<manager>:5000/topology/` path.\n\n  * **Parameters** : \n    * file: A yaml file that describes the application and the topology of the experiment\n\n### Undeploy Topology\n\nThe user undeploys his/her topology with a `DELETE` api call to the\n`<manager>:5000/topology/` path.\n\n### Deploy Actions\n\nThe user can execute various actions at runtime that can alter the underlying\ninfrastructure. To achieve that a user can execute `POST` call to\n`<manager>:5000/action/<action_type>`. For `action_type`, we have various\ntypes, namely: `horizontal_scaling`, `vertical_scaling`, `network`, `command`\nand `stress`. Users can determine either a `blueprint` `label` and the\n`number` of instances that the action would like to affect or the label along\nwith the number of a specific node, e.g. `supervisor.5`.\n\nWe have already described the action\'s parameters in `Actions & Scenarios`.\n\n### Get Monitoring Metrics\n\nReturns the metrics in CSV format for all instances of the running\napplication. The user should execute a `GET` api call to the\n`<manager>:5000/monitorings/` and the kresponse of the system will be in the\nfollowing form:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    {\n      "instance_id1": "CSV_file_for_instance_id1",\n      "instance_id2": "CSV_file_for_instance_id2"\n    }\n    \n\n### Remove Monitoring Metrics\n\nIn order to "clean" the monitoring metrics for a new experiment, we can\nexecute a `DELETE` api call to the `<manager>:5000/monitorings/` path.\n\n## Miscellaneous\n\n### Deploy a Network Distribution\n\nIn order to deploy a custom delay distribution, one has to capture a `ping`\ntrace file and deploy it to the system. Specifically, there is the `/generate-\nnetwork-distribution/<name>/` endpoint where users send the file through\n`POST` api call. The property `name` specifies the name of the distribution on\nFogify. The generation of trace file requires the execution of the following\ncommand where `destination` can be either a `url` or an `IP` of the\ndestination. After that user should store the results of the latter command to\na file. That is the file, which system requires in order to generate the\ndistribution\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ping <destination>\n    \n\n## Python SDK (FogifySDK)\n\nIf you are familiar with python programming language, we suggest to use\n**FogifySDK** since it has implemented all available Fogify methods.\n\n#### Read more\n\n__Monitoring FogifySDK __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/connection-3rd-parties.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Connection with third parties and API | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Instantiation\n  * Control Functions\n  * Actions & Scenarios Functions\n    * Actions\n    * Scenario Execution\n  * Monitoring & Analysis Functions\n    * Retrieve Monitoring Metrics\n    * Clear Monitoring Storage\n  * Miscellaneous\n    * Deploy a Network Distribution\n\n# FogifySDK\n\nFogify provides a python SDK with programming primitives for interacting with\nthe Fogify Controller. The FogifySDK provides the ability to submit IoT\nservice descriptions adopting the Fogify model specification, manipulate\nservice execution by applying actions and submitting "what-if" scenarios,\nextract real-time monitoring data and assess running deployments. Furthermore,\nthe FogifySDK has a set of built-in analytics functions applicable on\nmonitoring data, as well as, plotting functionality for easing metric\nexamination.\n\n## Instantiation\n\nUsers instantiate the `FogifySDK`, firstly, by importing the `FogifySDK`\nlibrary and, secondly, by created a `FogifySDK` object. The `FogifySDK`\nconstructor requires the url of Fogify `Controller` and the "fogified"\n`docker-compose` file.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    from FogifySDK import FogifySDK\n    fogify = FogifySDK("http://controller:5000","docker-compose.yaml")\n    \n\nThe `FogifySDK` object includes all required information for interconnection\nbetween the client and the `Fogify` framework. `FogifySDK` covers all possible\nfunctionality that Fogify API provides including control (`deploy`,\n`undeploy`), actions and scenario, and monitoring functions. The rest of page\nillustrates the latter functions and describes their documentation.\n\n## Control Functions\n\nControl functions are responsible for provision of a "fogified" topology.\nSpecifically, there are two functions, namely:\n\n  * `deploy` function that provisions, bootstraps and deploys a "fogified" topology. The only parameter of `deploy` function is the `timeout`, which determines how many seconds a user will wait until consider that a deployment has an issue.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.deploy(timeout) #  The default value of timeout is 5 minutes\n    \n\n  * `undeploy` function that destroys a topology and releases the occupied resources \n\nCopy\n\n    \n        fogify.undeploy()\n    \n\n## Actions & Scenarios Functions\n\nFog deployments are usually neither statically provisioned nor stable. This\ninstability highly impacts the execution of IoT services, especially in\nuncontrollable domains. As we described in previous sections of the\ndocumentation, Fogify addresses this challenge by providing runtime `Actions`\nand `Scenarios`. To provide a clear overview of actions and scenario\nfunctions, next we describe in details how a user can utilize `FogifySDK` to\napply them on a running topology.\n\n### Actions\n\nAn `Action` is a process that changes properties of a running Fog Topology.\nDue to extensibility, we introduce a general `action` method in which users\ncan utilize. As we described earlier, the method needs the `action_type`\nparameter, which currently could be one of the following:\n`HORIZONTAL_SCALING`, `VERTICAL_SCALING`, `NETWORK`, `STRESS`, `COMMAND`, and\nthe action\'s `parameters`. The `parameters` is a dictionary with all necessary\nvariables of an action and the emulated instance `label` that the action will\nbe apply to.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.action(action_type, **parameters)\n    \n\nSince the `action` method is too generic, `FogifySDK` includes a specific\nmethod for each action in order to ease their definitions and gives specific\nparameters for each.\n\n#### Horizontal Scaling\n\nA horizontal scaling action can either increase or decrease the instances of a\nservice (Fog Node). Thus, FogifySDK introduces two methods for that, namely:\n\n  * `horizontal_scaling_up` which spans new instances of a specific `instance_type` (is the same as the model\'s `label`). The number of instances is determined by `num_of_instances` and by default is `1`. \n\nCopy\n\n    \n        fogify.horizontal_scaling_up(instance_type, num_of_instances)\n    \n\n  * `horizontal_scaling_down` that destroys instances of a specific `instance_type`. Similarly, the number of instances is determined by `num_of_instances` and by default is `1`. \n\nCopy\n\n    \n        fogify.horizontal_scaling_down(instance_type, num_of_instances)\n    \n\n#### Vertical Scaling\n\nA vertical scaling action can either increase or decrease the processing power\nof a service (Fog Node). Specifically, user can provide the following\nparameters:\n\n  * `instance_type` that could be either an instance `instance-id` or `label`\n  * `cpu`, which is a cpu percent of increase (`+<percent>`) or decrease (`-<percent>`), e.g. `+20` or `-20`\n  * `memory` defines the new memory limit\n  * `num_of_instances` determines how many instances will be effected. The default is `1`. If the `instance_type` is an `instance-id`, the number of instances will not effect the action at all.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.vertical_scaling( instance_type, cpu, memory, num_of_instances):\n    \n\nThe method not allow definition of both cpu and memory vertical scaling at\nonce.\n\n#### Network\n\nNetwork alterations are crucial in testing of fog deployments, so, `FogifySDK`\nprovides a wide range of possible parameters that can be changed. At the\ndescription of Network QoS documentation, we illustrated all possible\nparameters that one can use in `Fogify`. Similarly, the same parameters can be\napplied at the `update_network` method. Specifically, the method requires the\nfollowing parameters:\n\n  * `instance_type` that could be either an instance `instance-id` or `label`\n  * `network`, which is the name of the network that will be updated\n  * `network_characteristics` are the network properties that will be updated from the action (same as `Network QoS` properties)\n  * `num_of_instances` determines how many instances will be effected. The default is `1`. If the `instance_type` is an `instance-id`, the number of instances will not effect the action at all.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.update_network(instance_type, network, network_characteristics, num_of_instances)\n    \n\n#### Stress\n\nA stress action provides the ability to simulate workload interference on a\nrunning Fog node. This is useful to evaluate the behaviour of a service during\nworkload variation and/or interference from other services. The parameters of\nthe function are the following:\n\n  * `instance_type` that could be either an instance `instance-id` or `label`\n  * `duration` specifies how many seconds the stress action will effect the node\n  * `num_of_instances` determines how many instances will be effected. The default is `1`. If the `instance_type` is an `instance-id`, the number of instances will not effect the action at all.\n  * `cpu` specifies how many cpu intensive workload threads will be spawed in the emulated Fog node\n  * `io` specifies how many io intensive workload threads will be spawed in the emulated Fog node\n  * `vm` specifies how many memory intensive workload threads will be spawed in the emulated Fog node and the `vm_bytes` determines the size of the memory that will be occupied and free in every cycle of the test \n\nCopy\n\n    \n        fogify.stress(instance_type, duration, num_of_instances, cpu, io, vm, vm_bytes)\n    \n\n#### Commands\n\nWith the `command` method, users are able to execute arbitrary commands\ndirectly to the emulated fog nodes. The latter gives the opportunity to extend\nthe functionality of Fogify without extending its code-base. The parameters of\nthe `command` method are:\n\n  * `instance_type` that could be either an instance `instance-id` or `label`\n  * `command` which the Fogify will execute on the emulated fog node\n  * `num_of_instances` determines how many instances will be effected. The default is `1`. If the `instance_type` is an `instance-id`, the number of instances will not effect the action at all.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.command(instance_type, command, num_of_instances)\n    \n\n### Scenario Execution\n\nAs we described in scenario section, scenarios are a sequence of timestamped\nactions described in a yaml representation. Users specify multiple scenarios\non fogify model file (the extended docker-compose) with different names. In\norder to execute a scenario through `FogifySDK`, you can simple run the\n`execute_scenario` method with the only required parameter to be the\n`scenario_name`.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.execute_scenario(scenario_name)\n    \n\n## Monitoring & Analysis Functions\n\nFogify stores the metrics from the running emulated nodes in a distributed\nmanner, on each host node. Users can then extract metrics to generate useful\ninsights about QoS, cost, and predictive analytics. This is achieved through\nthe `FogifySDK`, which retrieves local metrics to an in-memory data structure\n(`pandas` dataframe) providing exploratory analysis methods that produce plots\nand summary statistics. Next we have the basic methods that are implemented on\nFogifySDK to manipulate and user the stored monitoring data.\n\n### Retrieve Monitoring Metrics\n\n`FogifySDK` achieves the monitoring data retrieval by requesting them from the\nFogify controller. When the data is retrieved, the `FogifySDK` creates a\n`pantas` dataframe from them. Specifically, the method `get_metrics_from`\nretrieves all monitored metrics from a running emulated instance. The only\nparameter that the method needs is the `instance_label`.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.get_metrics_from(instance_label)\n    \n\n### Clear Monitoring Storage\n\nSince users would like to "start" different experiments without re-deploy the\nwhole topology, `FogifySDK` offers a method to clear the stored data. The\nmethod is the `clean_metrics` and does not require any other parameter.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.clean_metrics()\n    \n\n## Miscellaneous\n\n### Deploy a Network Distribution\n\nAs we described in previous section, users are able to deploy custom network\ndelay distributions. Specifically, user captures a `ping` trace file and\ndeployed to Fogify. The `deploy_network_distribution` requires two parameters,\nnamely, the `name` of the distribution and the `file` of the distribution.\nWhen the file is deployed to the system, Fogify is able to utilize it on the\nnetwork QoS properties.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    fogify.deploy_network_distribution(name, file)\n    \n\n#### Read more\n\n__Connection with third parties and API 5G-Slicer Extension __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/fogifysdk.html', 'title': '\n        \n        FogifySDK | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  *     * Features\n  * 5G-Slicer Overview\n  * Publications\n  * Acknowledgements\n\n# 5G-Slicer Extension\n\nExperimentation with 5G-enabled services over network slices is extremely\nchallenging as it requires the deployment and coordination of numerous\nphysical devices, including edge and cloud resources. To alleviate the\ndifficulties in setting up real-world 5G testbeds, we introduce 5G-Slicer\nextension of the Fogify framework. 5G-Slicer facilitates the definition of\nmobile network slices through modeling abstractions for radio units, mobile\nnodes, trajectories, etc., while also offering realistic network QoS by\ndynamically altering -at runtime- signal strength. Moreover, 5G-Slicer\nprovides an already realized scenario for a city-scale deployment that smart-\ncity researchers can simply configure through a "ready-to-use" template,\nleaving 5G-Slicer responsible for translating it into an emulated environment.\n\n* * *\n\n### Features\n\n####  5G Slicing Modeling\n\n5G-Slicer offers high-level modeling abstractions for 5G radio units, backhaul\n& midhaul QoS, user equipment, edge & cloud compute resources, VNFs, etc.\n\n####  Positioning & Mobility\n\nThe system provides positioning provisions and can alter at runtime the\nentities\' locations controlling in such a way the link quality, such as\nnetwork latency, bandwidth, error rate, etc.\n\n####  ITS Use case template\n\n5G-Slicer provides a "ready-to-use" template for a city-scale transportation\nsector that users are able to introduce their services\n\n####  Monitoring Capabilities\n\nSlicing plug-in introduced new monitoring capabilities for packet-level\nmonitoring and analytics to the emulation suite\n\n* * *\n\n## 5G-Slicer Overview\n\nA typical deployment starts by either describing the application services and\nnetwork fabric via the 5G-Slicer model specification or by parameterizing a\n"ready-to-use" testbed template. The model specification can denote a wide\nrange of network slice parameters, including the position of compute nodes and\nRUs, network links and their QoS, mobile node traces, communication protocols\nand VNFs applicable on nodes. On the contrary, parametrizable use-case\ntemplates automatically produce 5G deployments for IoT applications. The\noutput of each template is a programming view equivalent to a validated\ndeployment description. The topology and trajectories are propagated to the\ncontrol layer.\n\nThen, the system extracts from the description the network slice specification\nand any signal degradation models defined during the modeling process. With\nthese, it produces an in-memory Network Conceptual Graph (NCG), which contains\nthe aforementioned information and will be used by the system for the runtime\nstate propagation during the experimentation. The graph nodes represent\nnetwork and compute devices annotated with information about their\ncapabilities and deployed services, while edges denote the links between the\nnodes. The weight of each edge is determined by network QoS, incl. data rate,\nnetwork delay, packet and error rate. Then 5G-Slicer translates the NCG to an\nemulated environment by utilizing the Fogify Emulator Connector.\n\nThe connector is responsible for the emulation environment instantiation, and\nthe deployment of the IoT application through the FogifySDK. Furthermore, the\nTrajectory Manager parses the traces and applies the updates on the NCG, and,\nin turn propagates these to the running emulated environment. One can view\nthrough an interactive map the traces of mobile nodes, their performance (i.e.\ncpu, energy), and the load imposed to MECs.\n\n* * *\n\n## Publications\n\nFor more details about 5G-Slicer and our scientific contributions, you can\nread the papers of 5G-Slicer and a published Demo. If you would like to use\n5G-Slicer for your research, you should include at least on of the following\nBibTeX entries.\n\n5G-Slicer\'s paper BibTeX citation:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    @INPROCEEDINGS{Symeonides2022,\n    author    = {Symeonides, Moysis and Trihinas, Demetris and Pallis, George and Dikaiakos, Marios D. and Psomas, Constantinos and Krikidis, Ioannis},\n    title     = {5G-Slicer: An emulator for mobile IoT applications deployed over 5G network slices}, \n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 7th ACM/IEEE Conference on Internet of Things Design and Implementation},\n    year      = {2022}\n    series    = {IoTDI ’22}\n    }\n    \n\n5G-Slicer\'s demo BibTeX citation:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    @inproceedings{Symeonides2020,\n    author    = {Symeonides, Moysis and Trihinas, Demetris and Pallis, George and Dikaiakos, Marios D.},\n    title     = {Demo: Emulating 5G-Ready Mobile IoT Services},\n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 7th ACM/IEEE Conference on Internet of Things Design and Implementation}, \n    year      = {2022}\n    series    = {IoTDI ’22}\n    } \n    \n\n## Acknowledgements\n\nThis work is partially supported by the EU Commission through RAINBOW 871403\n(ICT-15-2019-2020) project and by the Cyprus Research and Innovation\nFoundation through COMPLEMENTARY/0916/0916/0171 and INFRASTRUCTURES/1216/0017\n(IRIDA) projects. The authors wish to thank Dr. Christos Tranoris and prof.\nSpyros Denazis of the U. of Patras for providing measurements from the "Patras\n5G" testbed, which was supported by the 5GVINNI H2020 (EU grant agreement No.\n815279)\n\n#### Read more\n\n__FogifySDK 5G-Slicer Getting Started __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/5g-slicer.html', 'title': '\n        \n        5G-Slicer Extension | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Start 5G-Slicer GUI and Fogify Backend\n    * 5G-Slicer & Fogify Services\n    * 5G-Slicer GUI\n  * 5G-Slicer Model Example\n    * Application Model\n    * 5G-Slicer-enriched Fogify Model\n  * Experimentation and Metrics\n    * Deployment\n    * Interactive Map\n    * Run Mobility Scenario\n\n# 5G-Slicer Getting Started\n\nThis page includes information about deploying a simple application on\n5G-Slicer plugin. Since we have already described the installation and\ndeployment pipeline steps with Fogify Framework, in this part, we provide\ninformation about 5G-Slicer instantiation and modeling. For more information\nabout the first three steps, you can go through our Fogify\'s Getting Started\nguide.\n\n## Start 5G-Slicer GUI and Fogify Backend\n\n### 5G-Slicer & Fogify Services\n\nAs we described before, one has to install the _preconditions_ of Fogify and,\nfor multi-host execution, to build a docker swarm cluster. Then, the easiest\nway to start the 5G-Slicer is to download its code from github repo, build the\n5G-Slicer container by running the following command:\n\n    \n    \n    docker-compose build\n    \n\nAnd then, user can start the 5G-Slicer in docker-compose mode by running the\nfollowing command in the project\'s folder.\n\n    \n    \n    sudo docker-compose -p 5gslicer up\n    \n\nEspecially, the `docker-compose.yaml` file of the project is the following and\nincludes both 5G-Slicer service and the Fogify services (Controller, Agent,\nMonitoring). We should note here that users need to define some parameters at\nthe `.env` file and can find them in Fogify\'s installation guide.\n\n    \n    \n    version: \'3.7\'\n    \n    services:\n    \n      ui:\n        build: .\n        image: fogemulator/5g-slicer-jupyter:v0.01\n        volumes:\n          - ./:/home/jovyan/work\n        ports:\n          - 8888:8888\n          - 5555:5555\n        environment:\n          - "JUPYTER_ENABLE_LAB=yes"\n          - "GRANT_SUDO=yes"\n        user: root\n        command: [\'start.sh\', \'jupyter\', \'lab\']\n      controller:\n        image: fogemulator/fogify:v0.02\n        entrypoint: [ "python", "/code/fogify/main.py", "--controller"]\n        volumes:\n          - /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock\n          - /usr/bin/docker:/usr/bin/docker\n        ports:\n          - 5000:5000\n        extra_hosts:\n          - ${MANAGER_NAME}:${MANAGER_IP}\n        environment:\n          CPU_OVERSUBSCRIPTION_PERCENTAGE: ${CPU_OVERSUBSCRIPTION_PERCENTAGE}\n          RAM_OVERSUBSCRIPTION_PERCENTAGE: ${RAM_OVERSUBSCRIPTION_PERCENTAGE}\n          CPU_FREQ: ${CPU_FREQ}\n          HOST_IP: ${HOST_IP}\n          NAMESPACE_PATH: ${NAMESPACE_PATH}\n          SNIFFING_ENABLED: ${SNIFFING_ENABLED}\n          SNIFFING_PERIOD: ${SNIFFING_PERIOD}\n          CONNECTOR: ${CONNECTOR}\n          MANAGER_IP: ${MANAGER_IP}\n          MANAGER_NAME: ${MANAGER_NAME}\n      agent:\n        image: fogemulator/fogify:v0.02\n        entrypoint: [ "python", "/code/fogify/main.py", "--agent", "--agent-ip", "${HOST_IP}"]\n        extra_hosts:\n          - ${MANAGER_NAME}:${MANAGER_IP}\n        volumes:\n          - /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock\n          - /usr/bin/docker:/usr/bin/docker\n          - /proc/:${NAMESPACE_PATH}\n          - /var/run/docker/:/var/run/docker/\n          - /sys/class/net/:/sys/class/net/\n          - /lib/modules:/lib/modules\n          - /sbin/modprobe:/sbin/modprobe\n          - /usr/lib/tc:/usr/lib/tc\n        privileged: true\n        cap_add:\n          - ALL\n        depends_on:\n          - cadvisor\n          - controller\n        ports:\n          - 5500:5500\n        environment:\n          CONTROLLER_IP: ${MANAGER_IP}\n          HOST_IP: ${HOST_IP}\n          CPU_FREQ: ${CPU_FREQ}\n          NAMESPACE_PATH: ${NAMESPACE_PATH}\n          SNIFFING_ENABLED: ${SNIFFING_ENABLED}\n          SNIFFING_PERIODICITY: ${SNIFFING_PERIODICITY}\n          CONNECTOR: ${CONNECTOR}\n          MANAGER_IP: ${MANAGER_IP}\n          MANAGER_NAME: ${MANAGER_NAME}\n      cadvisor:\n        image: gcr.io/google-containers/cadvisor:latest\n        volumes:\n          - /:/rootfs:ro\n          - /var/run:/var/run:ro\n          - /sys:/sys:ro\n          - /var/lib/docker/:/var/lib/docker:ro\n          - /dev/disk/:/dev/disk:ro\n        ports:\n          - 9090:8080\n        expose:\n          - 8080\n          - 9090\n    \n\n### 5G-Slicer GUI\n\nSimilarly with Fogify, 5G-Slicer provides the `SlicerSDK` (equivalent to\nFogifySDK). 5G-Slicer exposes the `SlicerSDK` capabilities via Jupyter\ninterface (`ui` service of the `docker-compose.yaml`). Furthermore,\n`SlicerSDK` offers a wide range of new visualisations (like interactive maps)\nand programming functions(e.g. move ad-hoc actions and trajectories). The\nfollowing image is a snapshot of the `SlicerSDK` jupyter-enabled interface.\n\n## 5G-Slicer Model Example\n\nNext, let us introduce a modeling example of an application.\n\n### Application Model\n\nAs we described in Fogify\'s getting started guide, users describe their\napplication via docker-compose files. Following yaml file depicts an example\nof a such application.\n\n    \n    \n    version: \'3.7\'\n    services:\n      cloud_service:\n        image: bus-exp:0.0.1\n      edge_service:\n        image: bus-exp:0.0.1\n      bus_service:\n        image: bus-exp:0.0.1\n        environment:\n          - "NODE_TYPE=IOT_NODE"\n        volumes:\n          - "/home/ubuntu/data:/data"\n    \n\n### 5G-Slicer-enriched Fogify Model\n\n#### Fogify base model\n\nWith the `docker-compose` to be ready, users need to add Fogify\'s extra\nfields, namely, `nodes`, `networks` and `topology`. The following example\nillustrates the high-level structure of an Fogify\'s infrastructure topology.\n\n    \n    \n    ...\n    \n    x-fogify:\n        nodes:\n            ...\n        networks:\n            ...\n        topology:\n            ...\n    \n\n`Nodes` are inherited from Fogify\'s model and there is no change in the\n5G-Slicer model.\n\n#### 5G Network Slice description\n\nIn 5G-Slicer, users can describe network slices, under the `network` field.\nSpecifically, a slice includes radio units (`RUs`) locations, `midhaul_qos`\nand `backhaul_qos` that are the QoS characteristics for midhaul (RU-to-RU and\nEdge-to-edge connections), wireless connection type\n(`wireless_connection_type`) like MIMO, and its parameters (`parameters`).\n\n    \n    \n      - network_type: slice\n        name: edge-net-1\n        midhaul_qos:\n          latency:\n            delay: 3ms\n            deviation: 1ms\n          bandwidth: 100mbps\n        backhaul_qos:\n          latency:\n            delay: 30ms\n            deviation: 1ms\n          bandwidth: 100mbps\n        wireless_connection_type: MIMO\n        parameters:\n          transmit_power: 30  # dbm\n          carrier_frequency: 28  # gigahrz\n          bandwidth: 100  # megahrz\n          UE_noise_figure: 7.8  # db\n          RU_antennas_gain: 8 # db\n          UE_antennas_gain: 3 # db\n          maximum_bitrate: 538.71\n          minmum_bitrate: 53.87\n          queuing_delay: 2 # ms\n          RU_antennas: 8\n          UE_antennas: 4\n        RUs:\n          - lat: 35.14996886033924\n            lon: 33.410295020090246\n    \n\n#### Topology\n\nFinally, users can introduce the `topology` primitive, which interconnects\n`services`, `nodes`, and `networks (slices)`.  \nSpecifically, a topology is a set of blueprint objects. 5G-Slicer extends the\n`blueprint` definition with the `location` field that could include\nlatitude(`lat`), longitude(`lon`), and altitude(`alt` in meters). Furthermore,\nusers should provide the `location_type` that is either `UE`(user equipment),\n`EDGE`, or `CLOUD`. We should note here that if the `location_type` is\n`CLOUD`, users should not provide geolocation, and if there is no RU at the\ncoordination of the `EDGE`, the system creates automatically an RU at this\nplace.\n\n    \n    \n      topology:\n      - label: cloud-server\n        networks:\n        - edge-net-1\n        node: cloud-server-node\n        replicas: 1\n        service: cloud-server\n        location:\n          location_type: CLOUD\n      - label: mec-svc-1\n        networks:\n        - edge-net-1\n        - internet\n        node: edge-node\n        replicas: 1\n        service: mec-svc-1\n        location:\n            lat: 35.14996886033924\n            lon: 33.410295020090246\n            location_type: EDGE\n      - label: mec-svc-2\n        networks:\n        - edge-net-2\n        - internet\n        node: edge-node\n        replicas: 1\n        service: mec-svc-2\n      - label: car-workload-1\n        networks:\n        - edge-net-1\n        - internet\n        node: car-node\n        replicas: 1\n        service: car-workload\n        location:\n            lat: 35.14996886033924\n            lon: 33.410295020090246\n            alt: 5\n      - label: car-workload-2\n        networks:\n        - edge-net-2\n        - internet\n        node: car-node\n        replicas: 1\n        service: car-workload\n    \n\n#### Trajectories\n\nTrajectories in 5G-Slicer extend the `scenario` primitive of the Fogify\'s\nmodel. Specifically, a trajectory is a sequence of moving actions that the\nsystem translates then into low-level network updates. For instance, the\nfollowing trajectory (`mobility_scenario`) moves the `car-workload-1` in\ndifferent location during the experimentation.\n\n    \n    \n      scenarios:\n      - name: mobility_scenario\n        actions:\n        - time: 10\n          position: 0\n          instance_type: car-workload-1\n          instances: 1\n          action:\n            type: move\n            parameters:\n                network: edge-net-1\n                lat: 35.15091624851098\n                lon: 33.408127726284306\n        - time: 10\n          position: 1\n          instance_type: car-workload-1\n          instances: 1\n          action:\n            type: move\n            parameters:\n                network: edge-net-1\n                lat: 35.15192942739787\n                lon: 33.405751258916474\n        - time: 10\n          position: 2\n          instance_type: car-workload-1\n          instances: 1\n          action:\n            type: move\n            parameters:\n                network: edge-net-1\n                lat: 35.15285486445768\n                lon: 33.40372880297997\n        - time: 10\n          position: 3\n          instance_type: car-workload-1\n          instances: 1\n          action:\n            type: move\n            parameters:\n                network: edge-net-1\n                lat: 35.15396009516559\n                lon: 33.401346833487295\n    \n\n## Experimentation and Metrics\n\n### Deployment\n\nThe following lines of code illustrate the use of SlicerSDK (which is an\nextension of the FogifySDK). Specifically, the user imports the SDK,\nconstructs a 5G-Slicer object, which encapsulates information about the\nFogify\'s controller url and the 5G-Slicer-enabled topology description file\n(`docker-compose.yaml`). Lastly, when one executes the `deploy` function, the\nsdk submits the description to the fogify\'s Controller.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    from SlicerSDK import SlicerSDK\n    slicer_sdk = SlicerSDK("http://controller:5000","docker-compose.yaml")\n    \n    slicer_sdk.deploy()\n    \n\n5G-Slicer displays a progress bar during the submission process.\n\nAt the end, when the deployment is over, the system generates a simple message\nto the end-users.\n\n### Interactive Map\n\n5G-Slicer provides an interactive map that depicts the positions of mobile\nnodes (blue markers), edge modes (red markers), and the network coverage (blue\ncircles). Furthermore, users can move the mobile nodes (blue markers) and the\nsystem will update the connectivity of the moving node.\n\n### Run Mobility Scenario\n\nThe mobility scenarios extend the scenario primitive of Fogify model and\nexecution. During the mobility scenario execution, the movement of the\nmobility nodes can be seen on the interactive map. When a mobility scenario is\nfinished, users can request the monitoring data via the start and end time of\nthe scenario. The following plot illustrates an example of network ingoing and\noutgoing traffic generated after the execution of a mobility scenario.\n\n#### Read more\n\n__5G-Slicer Extension Network Slice Modeling __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/5g-slicer/get-started.html', 'title': '\n        \n        5G-Slicer Getting Started | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content="Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin's Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  * Midhaul and Backhaul QoS\n  * 5G MIMO and SISO connectivity\n  * Mathematical Models\n    * Static Signal Degradation\n    * Step-wise Signal Degradation\n    * Linear and Logarithmic Signal Degradation\n\n# Network Slice Modeling\n\nUsers in 5G-Slicer are able to introduce network slices under the Fogify's\n`networks` primitive. The model of network slices include the `name`, which is\nthe identifier of the network slice, the `network_type` that is always should\nbe `slice`, `midhaul_qos` that is the connectivity QoS among RUs and Edge\nnodes, `backhaul_qos` that is the QoS connectivity between cloud-enabled core\nand edge, RU to UE connection type (`wireless_connection_type`) along with its\n`parameters`, and optional property `network_functions` of the network\nfunctions (or VNFs), that includes the Fogify's firewall rules\n(`firewall_rules`) and the packet level monitoring capability\n(`packet_level_monitoring`).\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    networks:\n      - name: 'slice_name'\n        network_type: slice\n        midhaul_qos:\n          ....\n        backhaul_qos:\n          ....\n        wireless_connection_type: ....\n        parameters:\n          ....\n        network_functions: # Optional\n          ....\n            \n    \n\n## Midhaul and Backhaul QoS\n\nFor the midhaul and backhaul qos, users can introduce network `latency`,\nincluding `delay` and its `deviation`, data rate (`bandwidth`) and the\npackets' error rate (`error_rate`).\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n      midhaul_qos:\n          latency:\n            delay: 30ms\n            deviation: 1ms\n          bandwidth: 100mbps\n          error_rate: 1%\n    \n\n## 5G MIMO and SISO connectivity\n\nFor MIMO(mutli-input-multi-output) connections, users are able to select\n`MIMO` (or `SISO` for single-input-single-output) as\n`wireless_connection_type` and to introduce specific parameters, like\n`transmit_power`, which is the power in `dbm` of the transmitter, the currier\nfrequency (`carrier_frequency`) in `gigahrz`, signal `bandwidth` in `megahrz`,\nuser equipment noise figure (`UE_noise_figure`), RU and UE antenna gains\n(`RU_antennas_gain` & `UE_antennas_gain`), the expected (or measured) maximum\nand minimum bitrate (`maximum_bitrate` & `maximum_bitrate`), the system's\nqueuing delay (`queuing_delay`), and RU and UE antennas elements\n(`RU_antennas` & `UE_antennas`)\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n        networks:\n          - name: dublin_network\n            network_type: slice\n            midhaul_qos: ...\n            backhaul_qos: ...\n            wireless_connection_type: MIMO\n            parameters:\n              transmit_power: 30  # dbm\n              carrier_frequency: 28  # gigahrz\n              bandwidth: 100  # megahrz\n              UE_noise_figure: 7.8  # db\n              RU_antennas_gain: 8 # db\n              UE_antennas_gain: 3 # db\n              maximum_bitrate: 538.71\n              minmum_bitrate: 53.87\n              queuing_delay: 2 # ms\n              RU_antennas: 8\n              UE_antennas: 4\n            network_functions: ....\n            \n    \n\n## Mathematical Models\n\nUsers are also able to select if the degradation of the signal follows a\nspecific mathematical model. Specifically, we provide four different models,\nnamely, `static`, `step_wise`, `linear` and `logarithmic` singal degradation.\n\n### Static Signal Degradation\n\nStatic (or flat) degradation model applies the same QoS in a specific radius\naround the RUs.  \nUsers have to select `FlatWirelessNetwork` as the `wireless_connection_type`,\nthe effective `radius` of the RUs, and the respective network's `QoS`.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ...\n        wireless_connection_type: FlatWirelessNetwork\n        parameters:\n          radius: 8km\n          qos:\n            latency:\n              delay: 5ms\n              deviation: 1ms\n            bandwidth: 10mbps\n    ....\n    \n\n### Step-wise Signal Degradation\n\nStep-wise (or multi-range network) connection has different QoS for different\nranges from the RU. For instance, the following description indicates that the\nQoS from `0 to 0.4km` will be equals to `3ms` delay and `10mbps` data rate,\nfrom `0.4km to 0.7km` will be `7ms` delay and data rate again `10mbps`, and,\nfinally, from `0.7km` to the radius the delay and data rate will be `15ms` and\n`1mbps`, respectively.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ...\n        wireless_connection_type: MultiRangeNetwork\n        parameters:\n          radius: 1km\n          bins:\n              0km:\n                latency:\n                  delay: 3ms\n                  deviation: 1ms\n                bandwidth: 10mbps\n              0.4km:\n                latency:\n                  delay: 7ms\n                  deviation: 1ms\n                bandwidth: 10mbps\n              0.7km:\n                latency:\n                  delay: 15ms\n                  deviation: 1ms\n                bandwidth: 1mbps\n    ....\n    \n\n### Linear and Logarithmic Signal Degradation\n\nFor linear and logarithmic degradation, users are able to select the\nbest(`best_qos`) and worst(`worst_qos`) connection QoS and the `radius`. The\nsystem will degrade respectively the QoS based on the distance between RU-to-\nUE by following the respective function.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    ...\n        wireless_connection_type: LinearDegradation|Log10Degradation\n        parameters:\n          radius: 0.8km\n          best_qos:\n            latency:\n              delay: 5ms\n              deviation: 1ms\n            bandwidth: 10mbps\n          worst_qos:\n            latency:\n              delay: 100ms\n              deviation: 10ms\n            bandwidth: 1mbps\n    ...\n    \n\n#### Read more\n\n__5G-Slicer Getting Started Dublin's Buses Use-case __\n\n", metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/5g-slicer/slice-model.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Network Slice Modeling | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n# Dublin\'s Buses Use-case\n\n5G-Slicer gives the opportunity for users to implement their scenarios via the\n`Template` class (`from usecases.template import Template`). Specifically,\nusers need to implement `generate_experiment` function or to utilize the\nalready created use-cases of the 5G-Slicer packet. The 5G-Slicer has already\nimplemented a city-scale usecase of dublin\'s buses datasets.\n\nUsers need only to introduce their application and a basic 5G-Slicer model\nlike the following:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    services:\n      cloud_service:\n        image: bus-exp:0.0.1\n      edge_service:\n        image: bus-exp:0.0.1\n      bus_service:\n        image: bus-exp:0.0.1\n        environment:\n          - "NODE_TYPE=IOT_NODE"\n        volumes:\n          - "/home/ubuntu/data:/data"\n    version: \'3.7\'\n    \n    x-fogify:\n      networks:\n      - network_type: slice\n        midhaul_qos:\n          latency:\n            delay: 10ms\n            deviation: 1ms\n          bandwidth: 1000mbps\n        backhaul_qos:\n          latency:\n            delay: 30ms\n            deviation: 1ms\n          bandwidth: 100mbps\n        wireless_connection_type: MIMO\n        parameters:\n          transmit_power: 30  # dbm\n          carrier_frequency: 28  # gigahrz\n          bandwidth: 100  # megahrz\n          UE_noise_figure: 7.8  # db\n          RU_antennas_gain: 8 # db\n          UE_antennas_gain: 3 # db\n          maximum_bitrate: 538.71\n          minmum_bitrate: 53.87\n          queuing_delay: 2 # ms\n          RU_antennas: 8\n          UE_antennas: 4\n        name: dublin_network\n      nodes:\n      - capabilities:\n          memory: 2G\n          processor:\n            clock_speed: 2400\n            cores: 4\n        name: cloud_machine\n      - capabilities:\n          memory: 2G\n          processor:\n            clock_speed: 1400\n            cores: 2\n        name: edge_device\n      - capabilities:\n          memory: 0.25G\n          processor:\n            clock_speed: 500\n            cores: 1\n        name: bus_device\n    \n\nThen, they need to select specific parameters at the `BusExperiment` class\nimplementation like: bounding box (`bounding_box`) in which the execution will\ntake place, number of RUs, MECs, Cloud nodes, and buses (`num_of_RUs`,\n`num_of_edge`, `num_of_clouds`, `num_of_buses`) that the system randomly will\nextract from the dublin\'s buses dataset, place of the traces file and bus stop\nfile, etc. Then, the function `generate_experiment` will return a `SlicerSDK`\nobject that already has the information about the deployment.\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    from usecases.dublin_buses_experiment import BusExperiment\n    from SlicerSDK import SlicerSDK\n    file_path = "<docker-compose.yaml path>"\n    fogify_controller_url = "http://controller:5000"\n    slicerSDK = SlicerSDK(fogify_controller_url, file_path)\n    experiment = BusExperiment(slicerSDK, \n                    bounding_box = (  # geographic bounding box of the experiment\n                    (53.33912464060235, -6.286239624023438), \n                    (53.35833815100412, -6.226158142089845)),\n                    num_of_RUs = 1,  # number of radio units\n                    num_of_edge = 1,  # number of edge servers\n                    num_of_clouds = 1,  # number of cloud servers\n                    num_of_buses = 1,  # number of IoTs (buses)\n                    time_to_run = 60,  # minimum time of a bus-trace for the bounding box\n                    traces_filename = \'usecases/data/all.csv\',  # file of the traces\n                    bus_stops_filename = \'usecases/data/stops.csv\',  # file of the bus stops\n                    edge_service = \'edge_service\',  # name of the edge service of the docker-compose file\n                    edge_device = \'edge_device\',  # name of the edge device (described in fogify model) of the docker-compose file\n                    bus_service = \'bus_service\',  # name of the IoT workload service of the docker-compose file\n                    bus_device = \'bus_device\', # name of the IoT device (described in fogify model) of the docker-compose file\n                    cloud_service = \'cloud_service\',  # name of the cloud service of the docker-compose file\n                    cloud_device = \'cloud_machine\',  # name of the cloud service device (described in fogify model) of the docker-compose file\n                    slice_name = \'dublin_network\', # name of the network that will be created\n                    max_num_of_trace_steps = 60, # maximum number of changes(locations) that a trace can have\n                    min_num_of_trace_steps = 0, # minimum number of changes(locations) that a trace can have\n                    bus_ids = [],  # specific bus-ids (traces) for the emulation, if it is empty, system takes `num_of_buses` randomly\n                    ru_overlap: str = "random"  # selects specific RUs based on their radius overlapping (`random`, `min_density`, `max_density`, `kmeans`)\n               )\n    slicerSDK = experiment.generate_experiment()  # builds the experiment based on user\'s preferences \n    slicerSDK.deploy()  # deploy the infrastructure\n    \n    slicerSDK.scenario_execution(\'mobility_scenario\')  # executes the mobility scenario of the selected buses\n    \n\n#### Read more\n\n__Network Slice Modeling Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs) __\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/5g-slicer/use-case.html', 'title': "\n        \n        Dublin's Buses Use-case | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ", 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content="Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin's Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  *     * Does Fogify provide workload generators for IoT devices?\n    * How Fogify achieves the mobility of Fog Computing Deployments?\n    * Where can I find examples of a Fogify deployment?\n    * Is the Fogify's emulation accurate and near to real-world deployments?\n\n# Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\nThis section demonstrate the most frequent questions along with their answers\n\n### Does Fogify provide workload generators for IoT devices?\n\nNo, Fogify only offers emulation at the infrastructure layer. Users are\nresponsible to provide workload generators as containerized services.\n\n### How Fogify achieves the mobility of Fog Computing Deployments?\n\nCurrently, Fogify provides users the ability to define scenarios for time-\nscheduled network alterations, so user should provide the network changes that\na Fog node will experience at the execution of the experiment.\n\n### Where can I find examples of a Fogify deployment?\n\nCurrently, we provide an end-to-end example of Fogify usage at the demo\nrepository (https://github.com/UCY-LINC-LAB/fogify-demo). However, we will\nprovide a wide range of applications described with Fogify in near future.\n\n### Is the Fogify's emulation accurate and near to real-world deployments?\n\nAccording to the emulation accuracy, we compare real deployments and emulated\ndeployments for the same architectures.\n\nOur experiments show the following results:\n\nThe emulated computing resources has only a small performance degradation for\nworkloads approaching 100% CPU usage\n\nFogify achieves near to real-world network link capabilities, with only\noutliers not captured and a slight overhead in low-latency connections\n\nThe emulation results closely follow the real measurements with a 5%-8%\ndeviation of the overall experiment time. The picture illustrates a image\nrecognition algorithm in two deployments. A Cloud-only deployment and an Edge-\nCloud deployment.\n\nYou can find more information about our experiments in the Fogify's paper\n\n#### Read more\n\n__Dublin 's Buses Use-case Installation __\n\n", metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/faq.html', 'title': '\n        \n        Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs) | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]
[Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  *     * Features\n    * Who can use the Fogify Framework?\n  * What can you do with Fogify?\n    * Topology Editing\n    * Deployment\n    * Testing\n    * Analysis\n  * Screenshots and Images\n  * Who is using it?\n  * Resources\n    * The Team\n    * Publications\n    * Videos\n    * Awards & Acknowledgements\n\n# Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework\n\nFogify is an emulation Framework easing the modeling, deployment and\nexperimentation of fog testbeds. Fogify provides a toolset to: model complex\nfog topologies comprised of heterogeneous resources, network capabilities and\nQoS criteria; deploy the modelled configuration and services using popular\ncontainerized infrastructure-as-code descriptions to a cloud or local\nenvironment; experiment, measure and evaluate the deployment by injecting\nfaults and adapting the configuration at runtime to test different "what-if"\nscenarios that reveal the limitations of a service before introduced to the\npublic.\n\n* * *\n\n### Features\n\n#####  Resources Heterogeneity\n\nFogify is able to emulate Fog nodes with heterogeneous resources and\ncapabilities.\n\n####  Network Links Heterogeneity\n\nControlling the link quality, such as network latency, bandwidth, error rate,\netc.,and even reproduce real-world node-to-node and node-to-network connection\ntraces\n\n#####  Controllable Faults and Alterations\n\nChanges on running topology by injecting faults, alter network quality,and\ninject (varying) workload and compute resources\n\n####  Any-scale Experimentation\n\nScalability from topologies with a limited number of nodes, capable to run on\na single laptop or PC, tohundreds or thousands nodes, running on a whole\ncluster.\n\n####  Monitoring Capabilities\n\nCollect, manage, and process metrics from emulated Fog Nodes, network\nconnections, and application-level information seamlessly\n\n#####  Rapid Application Deployment\n\nFunctional prototypes of an applications, written in docker-compose, demand no\nmodifications to its business logic in order run on Fogify.\n\n* * *\n\n### Who can use the Fogify Framework?\n\n####  IoT Service Developers\n\nwho wish to ease the testing of their services in geo-distributed fog\nsettings. With the proposed stack, developers design fog enabled services by\nusing Fogify to rapidly perform multiple tests and compare both well-\nfunctionality and performance.\n\n####  Academic Researchers\n\nwho wish to quickly assess algorithms for fog realms. Such users want to\nquickly perform their analysis over system prototypes, testing scenarios and\nfog settings, to discover insights without time and cost overheads of having\nto deploy prototypes over geo-distributed infrastructure.\n\n####  Fog Computing Operators\n\nwho wish to assess the impact of IoT devices to their infrastructure before\npurchasing and deploying to production.\n\n* * *\n\n## What can you do with Fogify?\n\n### Topology Editing\n\nA typical workflow starts with the user editing the docker-compose file of an\nIoT application, and extend it to encapsulate Fogify\'s model. The Fogify model\nis composed of: (i) _Fog Templates_ , allowing the description of _Services_ ,\n_Nodes_ and _Networks_ ; and (ii) the _Fog Topology_ , enabling users to\nspecify _Blueprints_. A Blueprint represents an emulated device and is a\ncombination of a _Node_ , _Service_ , _Networks_ , _replicas_ and a _label_.\nServices are inherited from docker-compose while the _x-fogify_ section\nprovides all Fogify primitives. Thus, users still develop their application\nusing familiar docker constructs with the added functionality of Fogify not\naffecting portability. This means that a Fogify enhanced description will run\nin any docker runtime environment without any alterations, however users will\nlose the functionality offered by Fogify.\n\n### Deployment\n\nWhen the description is ready, the user deploys the application using the\nFogifySDK through a Jupyter notebook, with the description received by the\nFogify Controller. If no error is detected by the Controller, it spawns the\nemulated devices and creates the overlay mesh networks between them,\ninstantiates the services, and broadcasts (any) network constraints to Fogify\nAgents. Specifically, the Controller translates the model specification to\nunderlying orchestration primitives and deploys them via the Cluster\nOrchestrator, ensuring the instantiation of the containerized services on the\nemulated environment. Located on every cluster node, Fogify Agents expose an\nAPI to accept requests from the Controller, apply network QoS primitives, and\nmonitor the emulated devices.\n\n### Testing\n\nOn a running emulated deployment, Fogify enables developers to apply _Actions_\nand "what-if" _Scenarios_ (sequences of timestamped actions) on their IoT\nservices, such as ad-hoc faults and topology changes. Actions and Scenarios\nare written by following the Fogify _Runtime Evaluation Model_. When an action\nor a scenario is submitted, the Fogify Controller coordinates its execution\nwith the Cluster Orchestrator and the respective Fogify Agents. Furthermore,\nFogify captures performance and app-level metrics via the Fogify Agent\nmonitoring module. All metrics are stored at the Agent\'s local storage and can\nbe retrieved from the FogifySDK.\n\n### Analysis\n\nTo create an end-to-end interactive analytic tool for emulated deployments, we\nexploit the FogifySDK capabilities in Jupyter Notebook stack. Specifically, we\npre-installed the FogifySDK library on Jupyter thus the user can (un-) deploy\na Fog Topology, apply ad-hoc changes and scenarios, and, especially, retrieve\nruntime performance metrics. For the latter, FogifySDK stores metrics to an\nin-memory data structure, namely panda\'s dataframe, providing exploratory\nanalysis methods that produce plots and summary statistics. Except of out-of-\nthe-box plots, provided by Pandas, we extended FogifySDK with tailored\nfunctions that provide a set of plots illustrating and explaining the effects\nof actions and scenarios in application performance. With the wide range of\nanalytic methods provided by FogifySDK, users extract useful insights about\nQoS, cost, and predictive analytics. Finally, users may integrate other\nlibraries, like scikit-learn, to endrose their analysis with ML and AI models.\n\n* * *\n\n## Screenshots and Images\n\n##### **Fogify Overview**\n\n##### **Fogify integration with Jupyter**\n\n## Who is using it?\n\n* * *\n\n## Resources\n\n### The Team\n\nThe creators of the Fogify are members of the Laboratory for Internet\nComputing (LInC), University of Cyprus. You can find more information about\nour research activity visit our publications\' page and our on-going projects.\n\n### Publications\n\nFor more details about Fogify and our scientific contributions, you can read\nthe papers of Fogify and a published Demo. If you would like to use Fogify for\nyour research, you should include at least on of the following BibTeX entries.\n\nFogify\'s paper BibTeX citation:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    @inproceedings{Symeonides2020,\n    author    = {Moysis, Symeonides and Zacharias, Georgiou and Demetris, Trihinas and George, Pallis and Marios D., Dikaiakos},\n    title     = {Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework},\n    year      = {2020},\n    publisher = {Association for Computing Machinery},\n    address   = {New York, NY, USA},\n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 5th ACM/IEEE Symposium on Edge Computing},\n    location  = {San Jose, CA, USA},\n    series    = {SEC ’20}\n    }\n    \n\nFogify\'s demo BibTeX citation:\n\nCopy\n\n    \n    \n    @inproceedings{Symeonides2020,\n    author    = {Moysis, Symeonides and Zacharias, Georgiou and Demetris, Trihinas and George, Pallis and Marios D., Dikaiakos},\n    title     = {Demo: Emulating Geo-Distributed Fog Services},\n    year      = {2020},\n    publisher = {Association for Computing Machinery},\n    address   = {New York, NY, USA},\n    booktitle = {Proceedings of the 5th ACM/IEEE Symposium on Edge Computing},\n    location  = {San Jose, CA, USA},\n    series    = {SEC ’20}\n    } \n    \n\n#### Other Related Publications\n\nA. Michailidou, A. Gounaris, M. Symeonides and D. Trihinas, "EQUALITY:\nQuality-aware intensive analytics on the edge", *Information Systems, Volume\n105, 2022, ISSN 0306-4379*\n\nM. Symeonides, D. This work is partially supported by the\nEU Commission through RAINBOW 871403 (ICT-15-2019-2020) project and by the\nCyprus Research and Innovation Foundation through COMPLEMENTARY/0916/0916/0171\nproject.\n\n', metadata={'source': 'https://ucy-linc-lab.github.io/fogify/#features', 'title': '\n        \n        Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework | Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n        \n    ', 'language': 'No language found.'})]

Actions and Scenarios\nare written by following the Fogify _Runtime Evaluation Model_. When an action\nor a scenario is submitted, the Fogify Controller coordinates its execution\nwith the Cluster Orchestrator and the respective Fogify Agents. Furthermore,\nFogify captures performance and app-level metrics via the Fogify Agent\nmonitoring module. All metrics are stored at the Agent\'s local storage and can\nbe retrieved from the FogifySDK.\n\n### Analysis\n\nTo create an end-to-end interactive analytic tool for emulated deployments, we\nexploit the FogifySDK capabilities in Jupyter Notebook stack. Specifically, we\npre-installed the FogifySDK library on Jupyter thus the user can (un-) deploy\na Fog Topology, apply ad-hoc changes and scenarios, and, especially, retrieve\nruntime performance metrics. For the latter, FogifySDK stores metrics to an\nin-memory data structure, namely panda\'s dataframe, providing exploratory\nanalysis methods that produce plots and summary statistics. Except of out-of-\nthe-box plots, provided by Pandas, we extended FogifySDK with tailored\nfunctions that provide a set of plots illustrating and explaining the effects\nof actions and scenarios in application performance. With the wide range of\nanalytic methods provided by FogifySDK, users extract useful insights about\nQoS, cost, and predictive analytics. Finally, users may integrate other\nlibraries, like scikit-learn, to endrose their analysis with ML and AI models.\n\n* * *\n\n## Screenshots and Images\n\n##### **Fogify Overview**\n\n##### **Fogify integration with Jupyter**\n\n## Who is using it?\n\n* * *\n\n## Resources\n\n### The Team\n\nThe creators of the Fogify are members of the Laboratory for Internet\nComputing (LInC), University of Cyprus. You can find more information about\nour research activity visit our publications\' page and our on-going projects.\n\n### Publications\n\nFor more details about Fogify and our scientific contributions, you can read\nthe papers of Fogify and a published Demo. [Document(page_content='Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulator Framework\n\n  * More from us \n  * __Fogify\n  * __5G-Slicer\n  * __\n  * Download\n\n  * ###### Installation\n\n    * Fogify in Docker-compose \n    * Bare-metal Installation \n  * ###### Getting started\n\n  * ###### Services\n\n  * ###### Node Profiles\n\n  * ###### Network QoS and VNFs\n\n  * ###### Blueprints\n\n  * ###### Actions & Scenarios\n\n  * ###### Monitoring\n\n  * ###### Connection with third parties and API\n\n  * ###### FogifySDK\n\n  * ###### 5G-Slicer Extension\n\n    * 5G-Slicer Getting Started \n    * Network Slice Modeling \n    * Dublin\'s Buses Use-case \n  * ###### Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)\n\n  *     * Features\n    * Who can use the Fogify Framework?\n  * What can you do with Fogify?\n    * Topology Editing\n    * Deployment\n    * Testing\n    * Analysis\n  * Screenshots and Images\n  * Who is using it?\n  * Resources\n    * The Team\n    * Publications\n    * Videos\n    * Awards & Acknowledgements\n\n# Fogify: A Fog Computing Emulation Framework\n\nFogify is an emulation Framework easing the modeling, deployment and\nexperimentation of fog testbeds. Fogify provides a toolset to: model complex\nfog topologies comprised of heterogeneous resources, network capabilities and\nQoS criteria; deploy the modelled configuration and services using popular\ncontainerized infrastructure-as-code descriptions to a cloud or local\nenvironment; experiment, measure and evaluate the deployment by injecting\nfaults and adapting the configuration at runtime to test different "what-if"\nscenarios that reveal the limitations of a service before introduced to the\npublic.\n\n* * *\n\n### Features\n\n#####  Resources Heterogeneity\n\nFogify is able to emulate Fog nodes with heterogeneous resources and\ncapabilities.\n\n####  Network Links Heterogeneity\n\nControlling the link quality, such as network latency, bandwidth, error rate,\netc.,and even reproduce real-world node-to-node and node-to-network connection\ntraces\n\n#####  Controllable Faults and Alterations\n\nChanges on running topology by injecting faults, alter network quality,and\ninject (varying) workload and compute resources\n\n####  Any-scale Experimentation\n\nScalability from topologies with a limited number of nodes, capable to run on\na single laptop or PC, tohundreds or thousands nodes, running on a whole\ncluster.\n\n####  Monitoring Capabilities\n\nCollect, manage, and process metrics from emulated Fog Nodes, network\nconnections, and application-level information seamlessly\n\n#####  Rapid Application Deployment\n\nFunctional prototypes of an applications, written in docker-compose, demand no\nmodifications to its business logic in order run on Fogify.\n\n* * *\n\n### Who can use the Fogify Framework?\n\n####  IoT Service Developers\n\nwho wish to ease the testing of their services in geo-distributed fog\nsettings. With the proposed stack, developers design fog enabled services by\nusing Fogify to rapidly perform multiple tests and compare both well-\nfunctionality and performance.\n\n####  Academic Researchers\n\nwho wish to quickly assess algorithms for fog realms. Such users want to\nquickly perform their analysis over system prototypes, testing scenarios and\nfog settings, to discover insights without time and cost overheads of having\nto deploy prototypes over geo-distributed infrastructure.\n\n####  Fog Computing Operators\n\nwho wish to assess the impact of IoT devices to their infrastructure before\npurchasing and deploying to production.\n\n* * *\n\n## What can you do with Fogify?\n\n### Topology Editing\n\nA typical workflow starts with the user editing the docker-compose file of an\nIoT application, and extend it to encapsulate Fogify\'s model. The Fogify model\nis composed of: (i) _Fog Templates_ , allowing the description of _Services_ ,\n_Nodes_ and _Networks_ ; and (ii) the _Fog Topology_ , enabling users to\nspecify _Blueprints_. A Blueprint represents an emulated device and is a\ncombination of a _Node_ , _Service_ , _Networks_ , _replicas_ and a _label_.\nServices are inherited from docker-compose while the _x-fogify_ section\nprovides all Fogify primitives. Thus, users still develop their application\nusing familiar docker constructs with the added functionality of Fogify not\naffecting portability. This means that a Fogify enhanced description will run\nin any docker runtime environment without any alterations, however users will\nlose the functionality offered by Fogify.\n\n### Deployment\n\nWhen the description is ready, the user deploys the application using the\nFogifySDK through a Jupyter notebook, with the description received by the\nFogify Controller. If no error is detected by the Controller, it spawns the\nemulated devices and creates the overlay mesh networks between them,\ninstantiates the services, and broadcasts (any) network constraints to Fogify\nAgents. Specifically, the Controller translates the model specification to\nunderlying orchestration primitives and deploys them via the Cluster\nOrchestrator, ensuring the instantiation of the containerized services on the\nemulated environment. Located on every cluster node, Fogify Agents expose an\nAPI to accept requests from the Controller, apply network QoS primitives, and\nmonitor the emulated devices.\n\n### Testing\n\nOn a running emulated deployment, Fogify enables developers to apply _Actions_\nand "what-if" _Scenarios_ (sequences of timestamped actions) on their IoT\nservices, such as ad-hoc faults and topology changes. Actions and Scenarios\nare written by following the Fogify _Runtime Evaluation Model_. When an action\nor a scenario is submitted, the Fogify Controller coordinates its execution\nwith the Cluster Orchestrator and the respective Fogify Agents. Furthermore,\nFogify captures performance and app-level metrics via the Fogify Agent\nmonitoring module. All metrics are stored at the Agent\'s local storage and can\nbe retrieved from the FogifySDK.\n\n### Analysis\n\nTo create an end-to-end interactive analytic tool for emulated deployments, we\nexploit the FogifySDK capabilities in Jupyter Notebook stack. Specifically, we\npre-installed the FogifySDK library on Jupyter thus the user can (un-) deploy\na Fog Topology, apply ad-hoc changes and scenarios, and, especially, retrieve\nruntime performance metrics. For the latter, FogifySDK stores metrics to an\nin-memory data structure, namely panda\'s dataframe, providing exploratory\nanalysis methods that produce plots and summary statistics. Except of out-of-\nthe-box plots, provided by Pandas, we extended FogifySDK with tailored\nfunctions that provide a set of plots illustrating and explaining the effects\nof actions and scenarios in application performance. With the wide range of\nanalytic methods provided by FogifySDK, users extract useful insights about\nQoS, cost, and predictive analytics. Finally, users may integrate other\nlibraries, like scikit-learn, to endrose their analysis with ML and AI models.\n\n* * *\n\n## Screenshots and Images\n\n##### **Fogify Overview**\n\n##### **Fogify integration with Jupyter**\n\n## Who is using it?\n\n* * *\n\n## Resources\n\n### The Team\n\nThe creators of the Fogify are members of the Laboratory for Internet\nComputing (LInC), University of Cyprus. You can find more information about\nour research activity visit our publications\' page and our on-going projects.\n\n### Publications\n\nFor more details about Fogify and our scientific contributions, you can read\nthe papers of Fogify and a published Demo.
